Xue Chuanfeng's Band Flees to Hebei

Jinan Dispatch: Rui Xiebang of the Propaganda Section of the General Staff Office of the First Army Group received a telegram yesterday from Rong Guangxing, the brigade commander of the 87th Brigade, from Puyang, reporting that the bandit Xue Chuanfeng's attempt to attack Puyang failed and he is now leading the remnants of 300 to 400 bandits to flee into Hebei Province. The banditry in western Shandong can be said to be gradually suppressed. He himself has led the History Corps to station in Puyang and will return to Yanggu within a few days. The original telegram is as follows: "To Brother Rui Xiebang, Section Chief of the General Staff Office of the First Army Group, Honorable Sir, Your humble servant led his troops to suppress the bandit Xue. We entered Guanxian on the 29th. The bandit had already looted the border and fled towards Puyang. Then, we received an urgent letter from Wang, the magistrate of Puyang, saying that the bandit Xue had the potential to attack Puyang. Your humble servant immediately led the History Corps to set off and reinforce Puyang. The army marched to Cangshang, but it was too late to pursue further. The next morning, we continued our advance and arrived at Puyang. According to Magistrate Wang, the bandit did not dare to enter the city due to the pressure from our army. He only led the remnants of 300 to 400 bandits and fled in desperation from Guyunji in the north of the county to Liuxiatun in Jizhou. This bandit, who was known as 8,000 and plagued western Shandong for nearly two years, has been collapsing along the way since our brigade besieged him in Yanggu and Shouzhang. Some were killed, and some were resolved by the militia. Now, there are only a few hundred left, who have fled our Shandong province to Jizhou province. The banditry in western Shandong can be said to be gradually suppressed. In addition to ordering the History Corps to station in the county, your humble servant will return to Yanggu within a few days to handle the affairs of clearing the countryside, in order to thoroughly eliminate the banditry and eliminate future troubles. I hereby report this to you. Rong Guangxing salutes." (3rd)

Results of the Preliminary Judicial Examination in Guangdong 73

Eighty Qualified Candidates Selected

Guangzhou Dispatch: The preliminary judicial examination in Guangdong Province was completed at the end of October. The examination was held on October 24th at the National Guangdong College of Law on Guangxiao Street. On that day, the chief examination commissioner, Yong Wenzhuang, the examination commissioners, Huang Jilu, the assistant examination commissioners, Cao Shoukun, Du Zhizhiuqiu, Xue Jixian, and the supervisors, Liao Yuzuan, Qian Yao, and Luo Baoyun, all arrived at the venue. A total of 121 people registered for this examination, and 117 people arrived at the venue to take the examination on that day. The examination time was divided into two sessions. The first session was from 8:00 a.m. to 1:00 p.m., and the second session was from 1:30 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. The questions for the first session were (1) essays and (2) official documents, and the second session was an examination of Party principles. All papers were submitted completely by 5:00 p.m. The results were announced on the 27th, with eighty people passing the examination, including Chen Xunrong, Wu Shuqiao, and Jiang Zhen. On the 29th, the preliminary judicial examination was held again. On that day, from 8:00 a.m. to 1:00 p.m., the subjects of "Civil Administration" and "Commercial Law and Regulations" were tested, and from 1:30 p.m. to 5:00 p.m., the subjects of "Civil Procedure Law" and "Administrative Law" were tested. On the 30th, the second session of the examination was held. From 8:00 a.m. to 1:00 p.m., the subjects of "National Government Organization Law" and "Criminal Law" were tested, and from 1:30 p.m. to 5:00 p.m., the subjects of "Criminal Procedure Law" and "International Public Law" were tested. After the two sessions of the examination were completed on that day, the preliminary examination was completed. The examination sub-committee sorted and sealed the papers of the first and second sessions and handed them over to the special commissioner Jiang Jiaxiu to return to the Examination Committee in the capital for review. After the grades were determined, the provincial sub-committee was notified by telegram and the official results were announced, so that the candidates could go to Nanjing for the oral examination. Problem of Prohibiting the Planting of Opium Seedlings in Southern Fujian 74

Zhang Zhen Requests the Anti-Opium Association to Send Personnel for Inspection

Xiamen Dispatch: Since the provincial government issued a strict prohibition on poisonous flowers in southern Fujian in the 17th year of the Republic, they have not been planted last year. This year, villagers in Zhangzhou, Quanzhou, and Xinghua counties suddenly spread rumors that the authorities were going to lift the opium ban. As a result, they purchased large quantities of poppy seeds and prepared to plant them. The Provincial Anti-Opium Association heard that some troops were providing protection. It reported to the provincial government, requesting that each army be responsible for prohibiting planting and not providing protection. On the 17th, Yang Shuzhuang sent a telegram to the leaders of the troops stationed in the province, strictly reiterating the ban. On the same day, Commander-in-Chief Jiang, based on the presentation of the National Anti-Drug Association, also telegraphed the troops stationed in Fujian, ordering them to be responsible for jointly banning planting with the county magistrates. If opium seedlings are found, they will be punished in the same way as local officials. However, according to investigations, seeds have been sown in Quanzhou, Jinjiang, Maping, Qingyang, and Anhai. In Nan'an and Tong'an counties, many seeds have also been sown. In Putian and Xianyou, planting is underway. In Zhangzhou, preparations are also being made for planting. After Chairman Yang telegraphed the reiteration of the ban, Chen Jiliang, the commander of the Marine Corps, immediately announced that his troops were strictly prohibited from providing protection. Zhang Zhen, the commander of the newly formed First Division, also telegraphed the provincial government, requesting that each unit send representatives to form a propaganda team to go to the defense areas for propaganda and supervision. On the 25th, he telegraphed the provincial government again, saying, "I previously received your telegram indicating the anti-opium measures. I replied by telegram and invited you to inspect. I, Zhen, am pained by the opium disaster. I have long heard of this decree. In the spring of the 17th year, I attended the provincial government meeting and strongly advocated the eradication of opium. My efforts were lonely, and it was even before the central government promulgated the anti-opium law. At that time, when the troops entered Fujian, it was the time when opium seedlings were harvested. Those who collected donations requested through intermediaries to pay hundreds of thousands of donations to delay the eradication. I immediately refused and eradicated them. The past is there to prove it. Now that the overall situation is calm, order is becoming more and more stable. Suppressing the Communists, clearing bandits, prohibiting opium, and eliminating drugs are all important tasks. Although punishing bandits and opium are three separate matters, they are intrinsically linked and should be taken into account together. At this time, when rumors are spreading that the ignorant villagers are secretly plotting to plant seeds, if strict prevention and suppression are not carried out, once the planting is completed, it will be impossible to enforce the law, and accusations will inevitably arise, accusing us of tacit approval and connivance. After careful consideration, I can only urgently hope that a special commissioner will come to supervise nearby and jointly form a propaganda team to achieve the effect of joint efforts. It is found that the former Director-General of the Anti-Opium Bureau often came to inspect in person. Now there is an Anti-Opium Committee, which is far away from the provincial capital, making supervision inconvenient. I also request that the members of the committee personally station themselves in southern Fujian to strictly implement the prohibition of planting, so that it can be known who is providing protection, the truth can be clarified, and the local authorities can also express their intentions. In addition to reiterating the ban and strictly ordering my subordinates to earnestly cooperate, I respectfully report this to you and beg your approval. Furthermore, Yunnan and Guizhou have relaxed the ban on planting, and Guangdong and Fujian have water and land connections. Prohibiting planting and transportation is especially difficult to take lightly. In recent years, foreign opium has invaded in large quantities. I hope that everyone will pay attention to it, so that the future of the opium ban may have a chance. Zhang Zhen bows in entreaty."

Crisis of the Jiguo Railway 76

Sharp Decline in Transportation and Difficulty in Covering Losses

Jilin Dispatch: The construction of the Jidun Railway was completed and opened to traffic three years ago. In the beginning, because the area of South Manchuria had just been developed and there were few passengers and goods, it was already making ends meet with difficulty. However, the losses were still limited. It was originally hoped that after a slightly longer period of time, it could gradually enter a better state. Unexpectedly, things turned out differently. This year's business has declined more sharply than last year, and it is necessary to lose about 70,000 yuan per month, which is almost unsustainable. The reason is that the road from the provincial capital to Dunhua passes through the three counties of Yongji, Emu, and Dunhua. Along the line, there are high mountains and ridges, and the trees are lush and vibrant, which is a natural and excellent forest, the so-called Huanghua Songdianzi Forest Farm. At the time of the road's planning, it was believed that the development of this forest farm was the basis of freight transportation, and it was expected that the transportation of timber along the line would be sufficient for the entire road's use. However, in the spring of last year, the Yongheng Official Silver Bank (Provincial Silver Bank) had a dispute with various timber merchants over the forest boundaries. The Bank said that the eight million square li of the forest farm under your management should belong to the Bank. The timber merchants argued that they held licenses issued by the former Forestry Bureau and argued according to reason. The provincial government ordered the Department of Agriculture and Mines to investigate and clarify that the former Forestry Bureau had made a mistake in re-releasing the licenses. After the Provincial Committee meeting, it was decided that the Department should jointly with the Official Silver Bank send personnel to survey the area. The remaining land should be given to the timber merchants. If it is not enough, it should be offset by other state-owned forests, and both parties' forest licenses should be recognized as valid in order to convince them. During this survey period, all felling was suspended pending resolution. The Department followed the order and sent technician Wang Qingsan to survey the boundaries. It has been one and a half years, and it has only recently been completed. The timber remaining along the line of the railway has already been transported. The source of freight has been cut off, and the income has been sharply reduced. Previously, the Official Silver Bank had been repeatedly requested to start felling as soon as possible in order to maintain the railway, but the Bank refused to do so on the grounds that it had been ordered to stop felling. According to the report of the Department of Agriculture, the area of the forest farm was surveyed to be 42,700 square li, which was allocated to the Bank. The amount still falls short and it remains unclear where the timber merchants should be compensated, so the provincial government still needs to consider this issue. Therefore, this case is difficult to resolve for the time being. The opening of the forest farms along the Jidun line will also be far away. The income from freight transport is even more uncertain. According to the Jidun and Jichang railways, the original director of the Bureau served concurrently. Since Han Linsheng was transferred to Tianjin Customs Superintendent, although there have been sayings that Cai Yunsheng or Yu Changfu and Qi Yao would succeed him, it has not been realized until now. This is also because Jidun is losing money and cannot sustain itself, and Jichang is affected by Jihai and can only maintain the status quo. No one wants to shoulder this difficult task. The road was built with Japanese loans, but no interest has been paid yet, so the name of the Engineering Bureau is still used, saying that interest is exempted during the engineering period. However, if this is delayed for a long time, the Japanese side may not raise objections. It is rumored that there is a saying that the loan should be recovered, although it has not been confirmed, it is not without reason. Moreover, there are often bandits hiding along the road who break the road works from time to time, causing no small damage. In the current state of the road, the future seems very dangerous. (October 26)

Shaanxi County Inspects Cotton Quality 77

Strictly Prevent Inferior Quality from Being Mixed In

Maintain the Reputation of High-Quality Cotton

Shaanxi County, Henan, is located east of Luoyang and west of Tongguan, adjacent to Lingbao. The surrounding areas are all cotton-producing areas. The cotton varieties are excellent and are the crown of all cotton in the country. It is also an important route for the export of Shaanxi and Bian cotton. Recently, large merchants from Shanghai, Hankou, and Shaanxi have pooled funds to establish a packaging company, which is about to open. This year's cotton harvest is abundant. Now that the new cotton is on the market, and with the war now over, large ports from Shanghai, Hankou, and Tianjin have come to set up trading posts for purchasing one after another. However, in recent years, cotton farmers and merchants have often mixed in inferior cotton. Often, good cotton cannot meet the standards when transported out. This year, the Shaanxi County Government and the Chamber of Commerce have established a cotton adulteration inspection center to prevent this malpractice. The regulations are quite strict. The following is an excerpt: (1) This office may inspect all cotton from Shaanxi County and cotton passing through the county to promote cotton merchants' self-awareness and strive for the purity of cotton quality to become the best product in China. (2) For cotton purchased by cotton merchants, after inspection, if it is pure and qualified, an inspection voucher will be issued before it can be shipped. A. Cotton with clean raw materials that is not wet or adulterated is considered qualified. B. Cotton is considered qualified if it does not have flower seeds attached during ginning. C. Discolored or purple cotton must be packed and received separately and must not be mixed with pure cotton; otherwise, it will still be considered unqualified. (3) Regardless of the buyer or seller, if the inspection result is deemed unsatisfactory, a re-inspection may be requested, but the reasons must be stated within 48 hours after the inspection. If the result of the re-inspection is the same as the previous inspection, the applicant must pay the inspection fee according to the package weight. (4) Cotton merchants must not receive or purchase cotton that has not been inspected. (5) If disputes arise in this office that cannot be resolved, the Board of Directors may be reported to hold a meeting to resolve the issue. (6) The expenses of this office will be deducted from the inspection of qualified cotton, with a deduction of five cents per package based on a standard of about 200 catties, which will be borne by the buyer. If the inspection is unqualified, the seller shall pay. (7) All buying merchants and flower merchants must trade fairly at the market price. The seller must not raise the market price, and the buyer must not use their strong capital to force the flower merchant to trade at a low price, causing the flower merchant to force the transaction, causing various malpractices to avoid the risk of compensation. Violators will be subject to penalties.

Zhenjiang Quick News 78

He Yushu, Director of the Department of Agriculture and Mines, has appointed Lu Feizhi and seven others to form the County-Level Chief Selection Committee, which was established yesterday.

Chen Tiaoyuan, Chairman of Anhui Province, was still sightseeing at Mount Jiaozuo yesterday and is scheduled to go to Nanjing today and then to Anhui to take office.

The Zhenjiang County Government has borrowed funds from the Zhenjiang and Baoyan Chambers of Commerce to build the Zhentan Road (Zhenjiang to Jintan bridge culverts) in order to complete the road as soon as possible.

The second local administrative meeting of Zhenjiang County has been extended to the 18th of this month.

The Dingfeng and Yongdingfengxiang silk factories in this port have been closed for a long time. Recently, due to the workers' request to resume work, the managers of the two factories have sent personnel to Anhui to purchase goods in order to resume work within the month. (5th)

Local Communications

Songjiang 79

Mud Beach Suffers Bandit Looting: Cases of banditry have repeatedly occurred in villages near Fengjing. Although efforts have been made to arrest them and sometimes there have been large-scale crackdowns, there are still lawless elements who keep popping up. The villagers are really disturbed by them. On the evening of the 4th, two bandit ships suddenly came to Mud Beach in the western countryside, full of more than twenty bandits armed with knives and guns. They broke into houses and looted, and the villagers were awakened from their sleep. They were watched and forbidden from making any noise. The bandits searched at will for about an hour, took the loot and boarded the ship. Before leaving, six men and one woman were abducted. It is said that the bandits spoke with a Tu-Ke accent, but their appearance could not be clearly recognized at night. The case has been reported to various agencies for investigation and rescue.

The Ministry of Finance's Anti-Smuggling Group Opens in Songjiang: The 2nd and 4th Anti-Smuggling Special Groups of the Ministry of Finance will be arriving in Songjiang by train this morning (the 5th). They will enter the city in formation and station in various temples and public places. All battalions of the 4th Group, 1, 2 and 3, have arrived completely. The group department is located at the old headquarters. Only part of the 2nd group has been transported to Songjiang.

Suzhou 80

Jiang Jigui Case: Prosecutor Appeals. Jiang Jigui, a worker at the Gongda Cotton Mill in Yangshupu, Shanghai, was sentenced to death in the first instance by the Shanghai District Court for killing Cao Buhua and inciting Liu Zijing to assassinate patrolman Wu Yanyao. Jiang refused to accept the verdict and hired lawyer Zheng Yuxiu to appeal to the High Court. On the 14th of last month, the Second Criminal Division opened the trial, which was presided over by Zheng Chi. Jiang Jigui was found not guilty of murder and sentenced to three years of imprisonment for the crime of possessing firearms and ammunition. At that time, Jiang stated that he would no longer appeal. However, after the judgment was delivered to the original trial prosecutor, Zhu Wenzhuo, the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau also submitted a presentation to the High Court stating that Jiang Jigui was indeed the murderer, and he had already confessed to the Public Security Bureau. Therefore, the Public Security Bureau also presented to the High Court, requesting that the prosecutor appeal. Now, Prosecutor Zhu notified Jiang Jigui yesterday (the 5th) that he had filed an appeal with the Supreme Court.

Lishui Murder Case: Appeal Heard. Wang Jianghan, a villager from Lishui County, injured his wife, Huang, in June. His father, Wang Buding, helped him strangle her to death with a rope. The Lishui County Government arrested Wang Jianghan and sentenced him to seven years and two months of imprisonment. After the verdict, the mother's family of the deceased, Huang, refused to accept the verdict and requested the prosecutor to appeal. The prosecutor filed an appeal with the High Court according to law. Yesterday (the 5th), the trial was opened by Zheng Chi, the presiding judge of the Second Criminal Division.

Jiading 81

Replacement of the District Head: Wu Buwen, the acting District Head of the Eighth District under the county, resigned. The county government transferred District Head Zhang from the Eighth District to fill the position. The vacancy was filled by transferring District Head Qian from the Seventh District. The vacant position of the Seventh District Head was filled by Ling Wende, a graduate of the Second District Head Training Institute and currently an assistant in the First District.

Female Student Rescued After Suicide Attempt: On a certain day last month, a young female student, carrying a bundle wrapped in cloth, arrived in Anting by boat from Taicang. She asked a passenger for directions to Huzhou. The passenger, finding her demeanor suspicious, questioned her. She said she was from Fuqiao in Taicang, currently a student at a certain school, and her family ran an oil mill. Unable to bear the abuse from her stepmother, she angrily ran away, intending to go to a classmate's place in Huzhou, etc. The passenger strongly advised her to take the same boat back home. The girl reluctantly and dejectedly returned to the boat. When the boat was near Qianmentang, she suddenly jumped into the river from the stern. Passersby noticed and stopped the boat to pull her out. Her bundle contained 2,000 cash. When the boat arrived in Tabu, the company reported to her family, who rewarded them with twenty yuan to take her back.

Wuxi 82

Unscrupulous Merchants Exposed for Selling Inferior Seeds: Yuan Hanchen and Zhou Meichun, unscrupulous merchants from Nanqiao Town, Third District (Yangming Township), manufactured over a thousand sheets of substandard silkworm eggs in Shanghai around September of this year. The printing plate used was of a mixed Japanese-Chinese breed. To dispel any suspicion from buyers, they privately carved a seal that read "Verified by the Sericultural Control Office of the Agricultural and Mining Department" and stamped it on the silkworm egg sheets. However, the character "Yan" (驗 - verify) in the false seal was mistakenly carved as "Nian" (捻). Yuan and Zhou, unaware of this error, concealed the inferior seeds in their luggage and transported them to Wuxi to sell them separately. The villagers who suffered losses were countless. Recently, when Yuan and Zhou went to Su Shuqiao to collect payment for the silkworm eggs, the affected villagers appointed Tao Zu'en (currently the chief of the Second Branch of the Qingyang Town Public Security Bureau in Jiangyin County) as their representative. They seized Zhou Meichun and accused him of selling inferior seeds. Zhou Meichun retorted, "If you say these are fake seeds, I can ask the Control Office to write a certificate to prove it." Tao Zu'en agreed and detained Zhou in the township, sending Yuan Hanchen to Wuxi to obtain a certificate from the Control Office. However, after arriving in the city, Yuan Hanchen, knowing that a certificate from the Control Office was impossible to obtain, requested someone (a certain Jia) to write a false letter for thirty yuan. Making matters worse, he mistakenly wrote the character "Di" (締 - establish) in the Control Office as "Ti" (蹄 - hoof). When he brought it back to the township, Tao Zu'en discovered the flaw. Tao charged Yuan Hanchen with three offenses: "selling fake seeds," "privately carving a seal," and "forging official documents," intending to send Yuan and Zhou to the county for prosecution. Subsequently, Wang Xuchu, the owner of the Hongren Silk Shop in Changkang Lane on the road, intervened. As a result, Yuan paid a fine of three hundred yuan, and Zhou Meichun had to sacrifice the seed price of two hundred and ten yuan, receiving no money back. He also spent thirty yuan on entertaining expenses for Tao, which helped end the matter of Yuan and Zhou's three offenses.

Old Woman Burned to Death After Knocking Over Fire Pot: The mother of Liang A'si, a resident of An'geng Village near Dangkou Town, Eleventh District (Nanyan City), was eighty-four years old. In the middle of March this year, she fell ill and was bedridden. Yesterday, her son A'si, because of the cold weather, placed a fire pot near his mother's feet for warmth. Shortly after, A'si went out to shop and locked the front door. Unexpectedly, his elderly and frail mother accidentally knocked over the fire pot, spreading the fire to the bed curtains. The flames quickly intensified, piercing through the roof. Upon hearing the alarm, the police officers from the Seventh Branch of the Public Security Bureau rushed to extinguish the fire, but the entire house was completely destroyed. A'si's old mother, unable to escape, perished in the fire, a truly tragic event.

Director of Education Lu Again Accused: Lu Renshou, Director of the County Education Bureau, has been repeatedly accused since taking office. Recently, more than ten local residents, including Xue Bingzhang, listed four major charges of embezzlement and malpractice against Chen Renshou and jointly submitted a petition to the Education Department. The accusations include fabricating observation notes, demanding ten silver dollars from the Education Bureau for travel expenses as a subsidy for his ex-wife Hu Lan'ying, and when his beloved wife Gu Jun Cui was the director of the Second Department of the Central Elementary School in the First District, Lu Renshou incited the burning of tuition receipt books and attendance rosters to embezzle over one hundred silver dollars in tuition fees and over fifty silver dollars in miscellaneous fees, and so on. After receiving the petition, Chen, the Director of the Education Department, issued an instruction yesterday: "Received. Will instruct the county to investigate and reply before further review. You are hereby notified."

Jiangyin 83

Reorganization of People's Organizations Underway: Sun Danchen from the Provincial Reorganization Committee and Wang Lifo from the Construction Department came to Cheng (Jiangyin) to guide the organization of people's organizations. On the 3rd, the County Reorganization Committee convened a meeting of the preparatory committee of the Chamber of Commerce. Wu Shuying reported that there were currently twenty-eight guilds being organized, and thirteen guilds approved by the Party Department were the earliest established, including the native cloth and factory cloth industries. Many doubts were raised about the provisions, such as the pawn industry, which only had five shops in Jiangyin and did not meet the quota for organizing a guild, and how to handle joining as a shop member without being registered. Committee Member Sun promised to submit a request to the province for interpretation. Also, the salt warehouses were government-established and commercial in nature but not registered with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Could they be shop members? Committee Member Sun promised to submit a request for interpretation and then send a letter to inform them. Committee Member Sun scheduled a discussion meeting with the cadres of the school self-government associations of various schools on the morning of the 4th and a discussion meeting with the representatives of the factory managers and workers in the afternoon. On the 5th, after inspecting the student self-government associations and various trade guilds, he would leave Cheng.

County Government Meeting on Cheng-Xi (Wuxi) Long-Distance Telephone Fees: Transportation between Cheng and Xi has always been inconvenient. In case of important military, political, commercial, or academic events, there is no other way to communicate except by telegraph. Jiangyin is also an important fortress. County Magistrate Li has repeatedly requested the Provincial Government's Civil Affairs and Construction Departments to expedite the construction of long-distance telephone lines between Cheng and Xi to facilitate communication. Now, the Construction Department has planned that it would cost seven thousand five hundred silver dollars, and the department needs Jiangyin to raise four thousand silver dollars. County Magistrate Li proposed how to raise the funds at the county government meeting the day before yesterday (the 3rd). It was resolved that the county government would work with the Construction and Finance Bureaus and the Property Office to raise the funds.

Zhenjiang 84

New Commissioners of Business Tax Collection in Various Counties Appointed by the Finance Department: The Jiangsu Provincial Finance Department recently appointed directors for the registration and collection of business tax in forty-three counties. The organizational method is that no separate agency will be established; they will be attached to the finance bureaus of the respective counties. The directors' salaries are set at three levels: one hundred yuan, eighty yuan, and sixty yuan. Each director will have three or two staff members. The names of the directors of all forty-three counties are disclosed as follows: Jiangning Ma Yuanda, Jurong Jiang Tang, Lishui Chen Yitian, Liuhe Chen Binghua, Gaochun Chen Fugang, Jiangdu Ding Buzhou, Yizheng Qian Enhai, Dongtai Wan Bingduan, Xinghua Li Naicheng, Taixian Cong Kuichang, Baoying Hu Baojing, Gaoyou Huang Hongdu, Wuxian Wang Shutang, Changshu Hong Sifu, Kunshan Yang Jichun, Wujiang Wei Cihong, Songjiang Cheng Jingchuan, Shanghai Hu Jiacong, Nanhui Shi Wei, Qingpu Liu Shicheng, Fengxian Zhong Ying, Jinshan Zhao Tingquan, Chuansha Ouyang Hong, Taicang Liu Boyang, Jia Yi Yu Shuxun, Baoshan Zhu Jianchu, Chongming Luo Zhenshen, Wujin Chen Naixun, Wuxi Zhu Shengwu, Yixing Tu Yuanran, Jiangyin Jiang Zumin, Jingjiang Gao Hongbao, Zhenjiang Wang Peishan, Danyang Wang Jilin, Jintan Tong Guangdou, Liyang Hu Aiqing, Nantong Zuo Shulin, Haimen Xu Lisheng, Rugao Kong Qingshou, Taixing Jiang Tingying, Huaian Cheng Zhaowu, Huaiyin Chen Naikang, and Tongshan Gu Shuwun.

Yangzhou 85

Brigade Headquarters Arrests a Large Number of Suspects: The command headquarters of the 133rd Brigade stationed in Yangzhou dispatched a team to Daqiao Town in the county area the day before yesterday and arrested seven suspects in a certain case: Huang Songlin, Yuan Ziwen, Han Fugen, Yuan Rongsheng, Ge Heshun, Xu Xilin, and Xu Jingan. They were immediately brought back to the brigade headquarters for interrogation and then transferred to the county court for punishment. Shao Songqiao Released on Bail After Paying Cash: It is learned that Shao Songqiao, the manager of the Wen Tang Bookstore in Duozi Waiti, in this city, who was arrested by the Jiangdu Public Security Bureau the day before yesterday for possessing a large number of obscene books, a total of seventy-one copies, and transferred to the court for punishment, was questioned by the Procuratorate of the court and ordered to pay a bail of one hundred yuan for release pending investigation and prosecution.

Page 10

The Pujin Ferryboat is Repaired and Resumes Service: The Pujin ferryboat, which travels daily from Zhenjiang to Guazhou, Shierxu, Siyuan, and other places, nearly capsized when it passed Liuxu two months ago because the river bank collapsed while it was approaching the shore. It was severely damaged and was sent back to Zhenjiang for repairs. It is reported that the repairs cost eight thousand several hundred yuan. The repairs have now been completed, and it will leave the dock and resume normal service tomorrow.

Large Sum of Money Found in the Corpse of Zhao Shisong: Recently, the Fengyu Small Ferry Boat of the Fuyun Company was robbed by bandits in Zhao Kai. It is now reported that Zhao Shisong, a passenger who was shot and killed by the bandits on the ferryboat, was from Xiaotanzhuang in the northern countryside of Yangzhou. He had been in the business of selling pigs. His wife has claimed his body for burial. He was found with a gunshot wound in his abdomen. Six hundred paper dollars and eighty silver dollars were found in his corpse. It is reported that this money was brought from home to buy pigs and that no pigs were lost.

Changzhou 86

Police Team Goes to Countryside to Suppress Bandits: Jiang Bingkun, the captain of the First Company of the Wu County Police Team, together with a platoon of military police, went to Panshu in the northern countryside the day before yesterday to suppress bandits. They arrived at Panshu at dawn the next morning and immediately searched for bandits in the vicinity. They captured more than ten suspects. After questioning them separately in Panshu, several people were released on bail by the township head and deputy guarantor. The police team and military police returned to the city at about 4 p.m. on the 4th, bringing back two bandits, including Zhang Rongsheng. After interrogation, they will be sent to the county for investigation. Also, because banditry in the northern countryside is becoming more rampant, the county government has specially dispatched Li Zongfan, the leader of the police detachment, to lead fifty officers and soldiers to Panshu Xiaoxinqiao on the morning of the 4th to take up defense duties.

Nantong 87

High Court Appoints Investigator: The High Court has appointed Wu Zhen, a judge from the Shanghai District Court, to come to Tongzhou to investigate the case of the Nantong County Court President Dong Banggan's lawsuit. He completed his official business on the 4th and left Tongzhou.

Piracy at Lvsi Increases: Six or seven hundred pirates entrenched in the Erjia Town area of Lvsi have recently gradually invaded the inland, burning, looting, and kidnapping. Merchants and residents within dozens of miles northeast of the city have fled.

Police Team in Haifu Town Rescues Hostages: Six pirate ships suddenly arrived outside the dike in Haifu Town. The pirates landed, but were intercepted by the Special Industrial Police Team. One pirate ship was captured, and hostages were rescued: Zhang Yizhong, Zhang Zhongxiang, Zhang Picheng, Shi Yuantai, two women, Cai Xuewei's four children, and one daughter of Zong Zhengtai, a total of ten people. They have been escorted back to their hometowns.

Problem of Riverbank Protection Expenses: The collapse of the Tongzhou Riverbank is severe. The Construction Bureau is rushing to carry out rescue projects at a total cost of over 16,000 yuan. However, a fundamental solution requires the construction of dike revetments, which would cost 300,000 yuan. In addition to using the additional land tax of three-fifths of a li, the amount is still insufficient. The county has requested the province to allocate funds for subsidies, following the precedent of the Jiangnan Pond Project.

Fengxian 88

Repair of Prison Expenses Settled: The original budget for the repair of the local prison was 8,000 yuan. Because raising funds has been difficult, the Third Committee has reduced it to 6,000 yuan and dismantled the Xiangcheng bricks and stones to build the prison walls to offset the cost. Zhou Jixu, the Director of the Construction Bureau, and the sub-office of the Second District have been appointed as the project directors, and construction is scheduled to begin today (the 4th). As for the method of raising funds, in addition to instructing each guarantee in the county to solicit five to ten yuan per chart, donation registers will also be printed to solicit donations from gentlemen and wealthy people.

Appeals After the Suspension of Two Chambers of Commerce: The Zhuangxing and Nanqiao Chambers of Commerce were ordered to cease their activities by the Party and government due to irregularities in the reorganization, and the chamber affairs were suspended. Now, the merchants in the town believe that the chamber of commerce is a gathering of merchants and should not be delayed, and they have repeatedly telegraphed the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to appeal. It is now reported that the Ministry has ordered the Jiangsu Construction Department to investigate and handle it according to law.

Jingjiang 89

Kidnapping and Ransom Case in Baimu Township: Chen Shite, a resident of Baimu Xiqigang Village, whose son Chen Kefang was returning home from Jiangyin due to illness, had just taken medicine and gone to bed on the night of the 2nd when more than ten bandits suddenly arrived and kidnapped him, bedding and all. There is no news of him now, and his family is extremely anxious.

Gaoyou 90

Wangying Town Looted by Bandits: Wangying Town, Gaoyou, was suddenly raided by a gang of over one hundred bandits last night, all armed with guns, and looted. It is reported that the guns and luggage of the military police stationed in the town were all looted, resulting in losses of about 100,000 yuan.

Principal Culprits of Riot Arrested in the City: The county government previously ordered Political Police Chief Jia Ziren and others to, together with five armed soldiers from the police team stationed in Yigou Town and two patrolmen from the Seventh Substation, go to Yijiazhuang to stop the performance of a play. Unexpectedly, the villagers of the village suddenly gathered and rioted, tying up Chief Jia and beating him severely, and confiscating their guns. Jia Kai and other political police who escaped reported to the county government. Zhou Qihong, Yi Bafeng, Yi Bacai, Yi Bagui, and other principal culprits of the riot suddenly came to the city yesterday. Jia Kai, the political police, spotted them in the Xihe Lane and arrested them all and sent them to the county government. Hu Cheng, the magistrate, opened a court to interrogate them. At that time, Chief Jia also returned to the city and testified that Yi Bagui was indeed not present, but Zhou Hongqi and two others were present and instructed [the riot], and I was tied up and severely beaten by them, and suffered serious injuries, etc. The coroner examined the injuries and confirmed that they were true, and ordered Zhou and the other three to be taken into custody first. Yi Bagui was released on bail pending interrogation.

Japanese Merchant Ship Sinks in Gaoyou Lake: Hengli Foreign Firm, a Japanese merchant firm in Shanghai, sent their partner Run Ting to various counties in northern Anhui last month to purchase 260 barrels of soybean oil and over 600 dan of sesame seeds, loaded on four ships. Unexpectedly, the ship encountered a storm and sank in Gaoyou Lake the day before yesterday. Fortunately, the more than twenty people on board were rescued by other ships. It is reported that the losses amounted to tens of thousands of yuan.

Rugao 91

Three Bandits Executed by Firing Squad: The county government executed the captured bandits Zhou Lianbao, Huang Shulin, and Wang Zhoushi by firing squad at 10 a.m. today (the 2nd), and announced their crimes.

Qualifications of Two District Heads Revoked: The Civil Affairs Department yesterday issued an instruction to the county government, stating that although Chen Weifan, the District Head of the Seventh District, and Chu Jiajun, the District Head of the Sixth District, had reported to the province, they had not attended classes. As such, they had violated orders and abandoned themselves. Chen Weifan should be dismissed from his post and his qualifications as District Head revoked. Chu Jiajun should also have his qualifications as District Head revoked to serve as a warning.

Sea Bandits Kidnap a Large Number of Fishermen: Chen San Mazi and Zhang Desheng from the Fourteenth Township of Juegang were kidnapped by sea bandits, as previously reported. It is now learned that their families scraped together 1,000 yuan and sent it to the pirate ship the day before yesterday to redeem Chen San Mazi and Zhang Desheng. On the same day, dozens of people collecting sea worms at Beigangkou Shakou were suddenly attacked by a large group of sea bandits and kidnapped over twenty people. The bandits instructed their families to prepare 1,000 yuan per person for redemption.

Captured Bandits Escorted: The Second Squadron of the County Police escorted to the county government yesterday the bandits Li Zheng'an, Tao Dekui, Huang Shengju, Liu Shuzhang, Li Jingu, and Gu Chengde, who were captured in Lizhuang Daichu. At the same time, 175 knives and one musket were also escorted to the county government.

Funing 92

Looting Case at Dongkan Tax Office: More than ten bandits suddenly arrived at the Dongkan Tax Office at 10 p.m. on the 27th of this month. They each pulled out pistols, threatening silence, and looted all the clothes, chests, and valuables of the officials. Then they escaped with the loot. After the Public Security Bureau heard about it, they dispatched a team to pursue the bandits, but the bandits had disappeared like a yellow crane. After the inventory, it was discovered that over 200 silver dollars and valuable clothing had been lost. It is reported that the director Wang Shanfu has issued a list of losses and reported it to the bureau for investigation.

Huzhou 93

Kidnapping and Looting Case at the Cha Family in Xiyang Village: In Xiyang Village in the northeast of Shuanglin Town, Huzhou, there is a certain Cha Xingjiang, a generations-old throat doctor whose family is well-off. In the late night of the 1st of this month, more than ten bandits speaking a Hakka accent suddenly arrived, each holding a gun, and broke into the house. They overturned chests and cabinets and searched wantonly, looting a large number of clothes, jewelry, silver dollars, and banknotes. They temporarily kidnapped Xingjiang's wife, Wu, and his apprentice, Cao. When the bandits were hitting the door, Cha managed to escape and injured his shin bone. It is now reported that the losses amounted to about seven or eight hundred yuan.

Pan Lanting Suddenly Receives a Bandit Letter: Pan Lanting, a farmer from Suzi Village, Du Xizhu, outside the west gate of this city, and his younger brother Pan Lanfa work diligently and thrifty and have some assets. Yesterday, they received a letter from the bandits demanding a large sum of money, limited to 1 p.m. on the 16th day of the old calendar to pay the money at a certain place.

Pinghu 94

Refugees Passing Through, Expulsion from the Country: A large number of refugees arrived in Xinhuang Town at around 1 p.m. on the 3rd, causing disturbances in the surrounding villages, forcibly seizing people's food, and resembling robbery. Shao Pincheng Sent to Hangzhou for Interrogation: Shao Pincheng, formerly a recruiting committee member, set up a recruiting station at the Yaowang Temple in this county in August, stealing electricity and beating people privately. After a brief interrogation by the county government's trial officer Li Cheng, he was temporarily detained at the county Public Security Bureau. Traces of Bandits Who Looted Zhoujiawei Town: Zhoujiawei Town, outside the east gate of this county, was looted by bandits on the night of the 30th of last month, with heavy losses. On that night, dozens of these bandits, all carrying box cannons, etc., first passed through Xinmiao Town, and from Yanqiaojiao, Ya Tou Di, to Banluoqiao, about half a li east of Siliqiao, and went south, all on foot. Residents along the way heard the noise and saw them with their own eyes.

Ningbo 95

Major Fire in Jiuqu Lane: A fire suddenly broke out in the Kong family's house at No. 6 Jiuqu Lane, Huxi, Yong City, at about 1 a.m. yesterday. The fire was very fierce and spread to the neighbors Lu Keming, Lu Adong, Lu Jinsheng, Zhang Yaoqing, Yuan Yiyuan, Dong Shaoshi, Ji Dairong, Lin Huisheng, Jin Changxun, Yu Guicai, Lu Dongping, and twelve other families, destroying a total of twenty-seven buildings, including buildings and flats. The loss amounted to over 10,000 gold. Fortunately, no one was injured.

Another Report on the Robbery of Ligang: A report on the full-scale robbery of Ligang Town, Fourth District of Dinghai, on the 31st of last month, has already been published in this newspaper. It is now learned that in addition to killing the security guard and shop assistants in this robbery, bandits also kidnapped twenty-four merchants and local gentry. Yesterday, the bandits sent letters to the families of the kidnapped, stating the ransom and contact points, demanding several thousand to tens of thousands of yuan. Education News

Important News

Students of Zhongda Discuss School Affairs 96

All Students Agree With Zhang's Resignation

And Discuss the Criteria for the Selection of the President

Nanjing, 5th: Zhongda students held a general meeting at 2 p.m. on the 5th, with over a thousand people attending. They resolved to agree with Zhang Naiyan's resignation as president and discussed and determined four criteria for the selection of the new president: 1. Has a reputation for scholarship and morality, and no bureaucratic habits. 2. Is dedicated to their work and has the determination and ability to develop Zhongda. 3. Has achievements in higher education. 4. Has a considerable history in the Party and the country.

Alumni Associations of Nanjing Higher Normal School, Southeast University, and Central University Advise Fellow Students 97

｜To Eliminate Opinions and Jointly Seek Improvement

｜Enmities and Grievances Temporarily Disregarded, Temporarily Compromise

The alumni association of Nanjing Higher Normal School, Southeast University, and Central University issued a letter to fellow students regarding the current school affairs dispute at the alma mater: "To our fellow students in the alma mater: Over two thousand students have graduated from the alma mater, both past and present. We have always maintained a consistent spirit of continuing the past and opening up the future. To promote the communication of opinions between students and alumni and to maintain the glorious history of the alma mater, the alumni association was born as a result. Since its establishment, the association has been in existence for over half a year and is actively carrying out major tasks such as investigating the service status of students in various places, raising funds to build a grand clubhouse, and printing and distributing association publications. The association is committed to achieving anything that is beneficial to the alma mater and to the students. This sincere intention is shared and trusted by the fellow students of the alma mater. Recently, the alma mater has unfortunately experienced disputes over school affairs. If school administration is neglected on weekdays, accidents will occur in an instant. When discussing the reform of school administration, some people want to take advantage of it. When discussing the movement to protect the school, some people also want to take advantage of it. Intrigue, sow discord, and conflicting opinions make it difficult to distinguish right from wrong. It is said that a certain organization or a certain student makes a statement that may not be made in good faith, but the conspirators are able to exercise their manipulative abilities to the extreme, and those who vent their anger only seek immediate gratification, using others as puppets, and the school has become their sacrifice. In order to protect the alma mater and respect the opinions of the students, the association does not want to participate in the debate. In the past, the disputes became more and more intense, which would inevitably shake the foundation of the school. The executive and supervisory committee resolved at a general meeting to put forward opinions for discussion with the authorities of the alma mater. This memorandum has been repeatedly considered and revised several times. If we dare to send it out, it is because the association has no grudges against anyone, but we hope that this solemn and brilliant alma mater will not be unstable and will not be taken advantage of by ambitious people, so as to fall into an unrecoverable position. To cook beans with beanstalks is not done by those who know. When brothers quarrel, they resist insults from outside. Now the school is in a hurry, and the ambitious will be complacent. The school is not private property, but they regard the school as a conquest. The alma mater has an excellent history, but they want to destroy and erase it. Those who have a conquering attitude or have other ambitions are not enough to blame. What I, a student in school or a graduate, cannot bear is that this solemn and brilliant alma mater is destroyed and trampled on. From now on, the association requests all students to quickly eliminate opinions, unify wills, and jointly seek improvement. All grievances are temporarily disregarded, and all factions temporarily compromise. Those who create happiness for our school should sing and praise it, and those who want to seek their own selfishness in our school should hate it. My classmates only know how to be for the school, not for others. The ancients said, "When doing something, do not be saddened by relatives and friends, but be pleased by those who see it." Also said, "If someone wants to do good, who is not as good as me?" The association is willing to encourage each other with the dear and respectable students. The alumni association of Nanjing Higher Normal School, Southeast University, and Central University."

Lü Miannan's Letter to Minister Jiang of the Ministry of Education 98

Lü Miannan's letter to Minister Jiang Menglin says: Honorable Sir, I received an anonymous leaflet a few days ago (I have already sent a copy for your review), consisting of over ten thousand words, vividly and meticulously describing how my actions over the past few years have all been under your direction, and wherever I am mentioned, you are invariably implicated. Such slander is not worth refuting. However, I now have something I wish to report to you, and I hope you will carefully consider it. Since you entered the political arena, you have been advocating the "Greater Peking University Principle." From Director of the Education Department to President of the University District, to Minister of Education, you have consistently used this policy as your sole means. Currently, the national and provincial universities within the reach of the Ministry of Education's power are almost entirely under your control. When you were in Zhejiang, almost all the principals of the provincial middle and primary schools in the province were from Peking University. Anyone from Zhejiang can attest to this. Peking University has a long history and naturally has many talented people. However, if you insist on using the name of Peking University as a rallying cry, maintain factionalism, and create an academic clique, then the bright and splendid history of Peking University will be smeared by your own hand. Thinking of this, I cannot help but sigh deeply. I still remember last year when the students of the National Teachers University sent representatives to the Ministry of Education to petition for the merger of schools. The students threw rattan chairs at you, and you relied on the protection of the military police, trapped in the building for a day and a night. I thought you would surely be furious and punish the students. Who knew that the next day you declared in the newspapers that the Ministry of Education had not offended the students, asking all sectors not to misunderstand, and hastily granted the students' demands, as if afraid of further action. You have been in Peiping for a long time and have experienced many student movements. You are like a bird startled by the bow, and I do not need to reproach you with righteousness. During the summer vacation last year, the authorities and teachers and students of National Central University strongly argued with the National Government and the Ministry for funding. On one occasion, representatives of the faculty and staff arrived at the Ministry. The students had arrived earlier and were talking in another room. After about an hour, you came and said to the faculty and staff representatives, "The funding issue has been negotiated with the student representatives." You then read out the various points loudly and said that you had signed it and given it to the students to take back. At that time, I immediately felt that your actions were very strange, as if your words and deeds had no credibility and needed to be guaranteed by your signature. Moreover, the faculty and staff representatives had repeatedly contacted you without any response, but as soon as the students arrived, you immediately agreed and signed it yourself to win their favor. Your intentions are obvious. Since returning to the country, from university professor to director of general affairs, to acting president, to director of the education department, to president of the university district, to minister of education, there are countless things that can be recorded about the words and deeds of students. I love people with virtue and do not want to embarrass others. The above two examples have long been known to the education community, so I cite them as evidence to make people across the country aware of your character. In short, the deterioration of the domestic academic atmosphere in recent years can be said to be caused by you alone, and it is not an exaggeration. Now that you occupy the highest position in national education, you cannot set an example for young people with a great personality, nor can you show the people of the country a plan for cultivating talents. You only know how to use means and play clever tricks. The future of education is still worth considering. I sincerely tell you this, hoping for your understanding. Respectfully submitted, wishing you good governance. Lü Miannan respectfully.

Jiangsu Education Funding Issue 99

The Finance Bureau Disapproves of Diverting Education Funds

The Education Department Negotiates to Allocate Previous Arrears

Chen Hexian, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, sent an official letter yesterday to the Jiangsu Education Funding Committee and the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office, stating: "According to the previous letter from your Education Funding Committee, the 21st meeting of the committee resolved to request the Education Department to consult with the Provincial Government and the Finance Department, ordering all county finance bureaus not to divert any education funds, regardless of the item of expenditure, and to implement the method of busy-season grain tax division. (1) Staff members of the Management Office may inspect the accounts of the county finance bureaus at any time, and the finance bureaus shall not refuse to allow inspection under any pretext. (2) The funds divided from daily income may be allocated at any time, etc., requesting that we take note and handle accordingly. We have already forwarded this to the Provincial Government for review and handling. Subsequently, we received instruction No. 7565, which stated, 'The submission has been noted. The Finance Department has been ordered to investigate the case and issue instructions.' You are hereby notified." In addition to sending separate letters, we respectfully request that you take note accordingly.

In addition, the provincial schools in Jiangsu jointly submitted a request to the Education Department, urging the Management Office to quickly raise and distribute funds due to the arrears in funding. The provincial schools in this city received instructions from the Education Department in the middle of last month, the original text of which is as follows:

"The submission has been noted. This Department is well aware of the difficult situation caused by the arrears in funding for the provincial schools for several months. In recent months, we have repeatedly urged the Education Funding Management Office to raise and distribute funds. Messengers have traveled back and forth, accumulating piles of documents. The Director of this Department has also personally negotiated in Nanjing and Shanghai. However, the amount of revenue is extremely weak, and raising loans has not been possible for the time being. We have exhausted our efforts, and we believe this is understood by all. Currently, the regular expenses for July have been fully issued by the Management Office according to the new budget. The regular expenses for August and September are still being raised with great effort, with the aim of allocating them in the near future to provide assistance. As for the temporary expenses for the 18th year of the Republic, we will consult with the Management Office to wait for treasury bonds to be used as collateral for cash before properly allocating them in accordance with the resolution of the Education Funding Committee. The temporary expenses for the 19th year of the Republic will be issued after deliberation and allocation."

It is also heard that the August expenses for the provincial schools have been received for half a month last week.

Resolution of the Jiangsu Agricultural Student Unrest 100

Fifteen Students Involved in the Trouble Expelled

Classes Resumed and Order Restored at 10 AM Yesterday

The details of the student unrest at the Suzhou Provincial Agricultural School have been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that after the incident occurred, the school principal, Liao Jianan, repeatedly telegraphed the Education Department for instructions. On the 4th, he received a telegram from the Education Department, informing the faculty and staff to handle the matter impartially and fairly, and ordering the students to resume classes immediately to avoid severe punishment. He also sent Secretary Huang to Suzhou to mediate. On the afternoon of the 4th, on the student side, because most of the students voluntarily resumed classes, the spirit of student solidarity dissipated. On the night of the 4th, Principal Liao convened a school affairs meeting of all faculty and staff. It was resolved that the students' actions this time were excessive, and it was decided to expel fifteen students who were the ringleaders. The rest who echoed them were given demerits. At 8 AM on the morning of the 5th, Principal Liao convened a meeting of the students in the auditorium of the Second School, announcing that the following eight students of the preparatory course of the Second College—Cui Fu, Zang Zhongchun, Jing Zhichang, Xiang Xuehai, Zhang Dasan, Zhou E, Shen Ruilin, and Wu Xixiang—should be expelled immediately for assaulting teachers and coercing a strike, with the most serious circumstances, and were required to leave the school immediately. The following nine students—Pan Xikang, Li Hongxun, Hua YouNian, Song Fengzhai, Chu Fusheng, Zhu Jingyuan, Xu Zhengshi, Jin Fa, Ye Haokui—were each given two major demerits. The following six students—Wang Qinghao, Fu Zhengfu, Zhang Guoji, Zhao Tashou, Fang Zhenzhong, Xie Jingyuan—were each given one major demerit. Yang Baisong confessed and reported the instigators of the unrest and was given one major demerit as a lenient punishment. The following seven students of the undergraduate course of the First College—Zhao Chuanxu, Sheng Hua, He Sennian, Zhang Shu, Zhou Zhiang, Zeng Yuanpei, Wang Hanxiong—should be expelled for echoing the student unrest and assaulting teachers under false pretenses. Wu Tingchen was given two major demerits as a lenient punishment. Zhang Hancai and Deng Jinpeng were each given one major demerit and two minor demerits. Jiang Yintang was given one major demerit and one minor demerit. The rest of the students who blindly followed were all given lenient exemptions from punishment. The students present did not resist and voluntarily resumed classes, signing their names one after another. Classes resumed at 10 AM. The expelled students left the school immediately. Principal Liao informed the county government of the events that day and reported to the Education Department. However, Xiang Xuehai and Zhou Mou, who were expelled, had gone to the province to report to the Education Department the day before. There are probably no major problems. However, after Dai Qixiang, the director of the preparatory course of the Second College, was dismissed, it is heard that the school authorities plan to no longer establish a director of the preparatory course and will instead appoint two dormitory administrators to be fully responsible for student management.

Soochow University's Explanation Regarding Shanghai University's Suspension of the Jiangnan University Tennis Tournament 110

Xu Minhui, Director of the Soochow University Sports Publication, sent a letter yesterday regarding Shanghai University's suspension of the Jiangnan University tennis match. The original letter is recorded below:

To the Editor of the Sports Column of the Shanghai News Education News: I read the statement published in your newspaper on November 2nd regarding the suspension of the Shanghai University competition. The letter from Mr. Ni Xiaotong, Sports Instructor of Shanghai University, to your newspaper, states reasons that violate the regulations and deviate from the facts. He judges with his own intentions and uses them as the association's regulations. He was not present at the time and assumes that the situation was as such. This is inevitably self-deceptive, so I must provide a more detailed explanation to avoid misunderstandings among those who sympathize with the sports community. Therefore, I will explain and refute it in detail below:

1. The original letter states, "According to the charter of the East China Four University Sports Association, if it rains during a ball game, the game may be postponed if both parties agree. If one party does not agree, the game must still proceed." I have served as the chairman of the association for a year and am currently the secretary. I have read the association's charter thoroughly from beginning to end, but I have never seen the statement "If it rains during a ball game, the game may be postponed if both parties agree. If one party does not agree, the game must still proceed." I do not know where Mr. Ni Xiaotong's statement comes from. Where was the charter of the Four University Sports Association printed? I am not talented, but I respectfully ask Mr. Ni to point it out.

2. The letter also states, "After the first game ended, the referee immediately negotiated with the physical education instructor and players from Jinling University and decided to stop the game. Afterwards, the referee and the Jinling players left the field." I do not know if Mr. Ni's statement is based on fantasy or on the words of one or two students. To state so boldly, "The referee and the physical education instructor and players from Jinling University negotiated and decided to stop the game. Afterwards, the referee and the Jinling players left the field." It is not known that when the game began, the Shanghai University physical education instructor, Mr. Ni, could not be found. The officers, captains, and team members did not know where he was. They had no choice but to have the officer act on his behalf, appointing scorers and linesmen, and then begin the game. When the first game ended, it was pouring rain. The referee first asked Mr. Xu Shaowu, the instructor from Shanghai University, under a large tree, whether to continue the game. The Shanghai University representative agreed to continue the game, but the Jinling University representative believed that the rain and mud had soaked both teams and that they were slipping and falling on the ground, so for the sake of both teams' health, he did not agree to continue the game and asked to postpone it to the morning of November 1st (Saturday). At that time, the judge saw that both sides were deadlocked, so he asked the chairman to convene a special meeting to resolve it. Chairman Xu Shaowu again searched for the Shanghai University physical education instructor but still could not find him. He was forced to have Mr. Yu Tingzhi, the officer of the school, attend as a representative. After a long discussion, Mr. Zhu Peien, the representative from Zhijiang University, cited the volleyball competition held in Shanghai University last year, which was also disrupted by rain. Jinling University asked to stop the game, but Soochow University opposed it, so the meeting decided to postpone it and continue the next morning. There was an example to follow, so it was proposed that there was no need to discuss it further and that the competition should be postponed according to last year's method. If it was still raining the next day, it would be held in the Jinghai Literary Fitness Room. At this point, there was no objection, so it was passed. At this time, Mr. Ni Xiaotong came slowly, and the meeting informed Mr. Ni of the resolution. Mr. Ni then said that if the members had returned and the meeting had decided to hold the competition, then Shanghai University would have to forfeit. Moreover, the sports reporter Mr. Pei from the News Newspaper of Suzhou and a reporter from a certain newspaper were present throughout the meeting. Therefore, it is unclear where Mr. Ni's statements came from. (To be continued)

Special Publication

The Question of the Concession's Department of Education (Zhou Shang) 111

Two years ago, I wrote an article for the "Student Lamp" section of the Times News, titled "Shanghai Education," in which I stated that the recovery of the educational rights of the concessions should be immediate. Unexpectedly, the goal has not been achieved, and the other party suddenly announced the establishment of a Department of Education. The Ministry of Education is the highest administrative organ of education in our country. This move by the Shanghai Municipal Council not only disrupts our country's education system but also insults our national dignity. How can this be tolerated? I spent a week investigating the Shanghai Municipal Council's facilities for education in the Public Concession and the emergence of its Department of Education. I respectfully present the information I have gathered in this article to the people of the country.

The Loss of Educational Rights and the Overview of Concession Education 112

Educational rights are inherently national rights. Those who provide education do so with the welfare of the community as the prerequisite, and those who receive education must also learn the customs and traditions of the community and abide by its rules in order to join the community. People form a country through the combination of living habits and environmental aspects over a long history. In order to consolidate the foundation of the country and develop culture, the country adopts certain goals and policies for national education. All people under the control of the country must be subject to its control and proceed according to its direction. This right to education is unique to the country, so it is called national right. With national rights, we have the right to formulate educational aims, educational policies, educational supervision, educational decision-making, etc.

Our country's educational rights have been lost for many years. The reasons for the loss of rights are: 1. The proliferation of missionary schools throughout the country. 2. The establishment of colonial schools. Various concessions and the three northeastern provinces are the most notable. The first reason stems from the introduction of Christianity into the Central Plains in the ninth year of the Zhenguan era of the Tang Dynasty, which was a scourge. China was defeated by England and then by the Anglo-French alliance. The Treaty of Nanjing and the Treaty of Tianjin were successively established. The power of Christianity was unapproachable. In the thirty-second year of Guangxu, the Ministry of Education promulgated that foreigners setting up schools did not need to register, planting the seeds of disaster and causing endless harm. The second reason is the concessions and the Russo-Japanese War. After the war, Japan obtained Lushun, and the South Manchurian Railway connected to the Beining Railway, reaching the area directly. The Japanese then expanded from Lushun to the South Manchurian Railway line and extended it to the provincial capital of Fengtian, receiving Chinese children and educating them on their behalf. The purpose was to cultivate obedient subjects and servants to be used by the Japanese. We must recognize that the former type of educational right was abandoned by the Chinese themselves, with no treaty provisions. The latter type of loss of educational rights was mainly due to unequal treaties.

The educational rights of the Shanghai Public Concession include the above two types. The Chinese Public School, Yucai Public School, Gezhi Public School, and Nie Zhongcheng Public School established by the Shanghai Municipal Council are colonial schools. St. Francis, St. Mary's, McLaren, etc., belong to missionary schools. Missionary schools aim primarily at proselytizing and aggression, while colonial schools aim primarily at cultivating obedient subjects. Neither is Chinese education. They hinder our country's educational rights and are sufficient to destroy our country's culture. The Shanghai Municipal Council's recent establishment of a Chinese Education Office to manage the newly established Chinese primary schools in the West and East Districts is just window dressing.

The four public schools within the concession are poorly managed. School administration shifts with personnel changes. All facilities do not contain national characteristics. The curriculum emphasizes English and lacks science. Discipline emphasizes corporal punishment and obedience, despising individuality. Most students go to work for foreigners. It is rarely heard that graduates of these public schools occupy important positions in Chinese society. My younger brother once studied at Yucai Public School on Shanhai Pass Road for three years. Later, he was interfered with by the authorities due to the May Fourth Movement and dropped out of school. Since then, Yucai has not accepted students over the age of sixteen, and tuition has increased to more than forty yuan. The intentions of Sima Zhao are obvious to everyone. Other issues, such as the excessive number of schools and the fact that funding accounts for only 1.07% of the city's revenue, will not be discussed due to limited space.

The Ministry of Education and the Education Office 113

Recently, the discovery of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Department of Education has attracted the attention of the Chinese people. I met with Chen Heqin, Director of the Chinese Education Office, and one or two Chinese members of the Taxpayers' Association. According to them, the Shanghai Municipal Council's Educational Department, translated into Chinese as "Ministry of Education," is listed alongside the Police Department and the Engineering Department. It has been established for more than sixty years, but it has little contact with the outside world, especially with us Chinese, so few people outside know about it. Its organization has a secretary, and the secretary hires an assistant who specializes in the four public schools for Chinese education. It was felt that the administration was not unified and that the assistant was tired of the tedious affairs, so the Department of Education was changed to the Education Office, and Healey was hired as the director to manage all education within the concession. This is evidenced by the fourth issue of the Chinese Weekly published by the Shanghai Municipal Council in April of the previous year. However, the Shanghai Municipal Council's organization is all named after departments, but education is not, which is inevitably suspicious. Chen told me that the change from "Department" to "Office" is indeed a fact but has not been formally approved. It is expected that in the near future, the Shanghai Municipal Council will uniformly change to "Office," at which time it can be formally announced to avoid conflicts with the government agencies of our country. (To be continued)
