National Industry and Commerce Conference Special Issue No. 6

Fifth Day of the Industry and Commerce Conference 114

Fourth General Meeting Passes Reports of Groups 3, 4, and 5

Implementation of the Labor-Management Cooperation Plan Also Passed Yesterday

Decisions on Basic Industries, Indigenous Industries, and Important Cases

Suppression of Prize Savings Associations, Please Draft Methods by the Ministries of Industry and Finance

Fourth General Meeting Yesterday

Presidium Report 115

A Total of 405 Proposals Received

The fourth general meeting of the National Industry and Commerce Conference was held at the Lizhi Society at 2 PM on the 5th. Chairman Kong Xiangxi, Vice-Chairmen Mu Xiangyue and Zheng Hongnian, and four members of the presidium, Ma Chaojun, Hu Shuhua, Ren Sida, and Xu Jiyu, and 135 members, including Wang Xiaolai, attended. Chairman Mu Xiangyue reported that the deadline for submitting proposals to the conference was the 5th. A total of 405 proposals had been received. A total of 221 proposals had been reviewed and reported, 105 proposals had not been reviewed, and 79 proposals had been passed. There are only three days left until the closing date. It is hoped that everyone will work hard to pass all the proposals as scheduled.

Regarding the Adoption of a Labor-Management Cooperation Plan 116

Report

Following the report, the meeting commenced according to the agenda. First, Hu Shuhua reported on the first case of the third group, which was the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's proposed plan for realizing labor-management cooperation. This morning at 9:00 AM, the review committee of this group and the chairmen and members of each group, totaling 57 people, convened to re-examine the results and amend the various points, and then read the full report as follows:

The following amendments should be made to this proposal. In recent years, factory owners and employees in various regions have frequently experienced disputes due to conflicting interests. In minor cases, production is reduced; in severe cases, factories are shut down, leading to a sharp increase in unemployment. This not only hinders the development of various industries but also affects social stability. The Ministry, in order to realize labor-management cooperation and develop the national economy, now proposes the following plan for whether it is applicable, please submit it for public decision.

1. Both employers and employees must understand the following matters: (1) Factories are profit-generating institutions that both parties rely on for their livelihoods. (2) Factories are places that produce goods to meet the needs of society. (3) The relationship between the two parties is like that of brothers and cannot be separated. Occasional labor disputes, even if unintentional, cause losses to both employers and employees and also affect society. (4) The right to manage the factory is a legitimate function of the factory management.

2. Labor-management contracts must be signed jointly by an equal number of representatives from both parties and reported to the local government for record.

3. The aforementioned contract shall specify the following items: (1) Working hours and methods of compensating for extended working hours. (2) Wage amounts and their payment. (3) Methods of rewards and punishments. (4) The start and end dates of the contract's validity. (5) Whether the contract can be amended by either party before the expiration date. (6) The location and date of the contract signing. (7) The names of the contract signatories. (8) Matters related to local labor-management customs. (9) Other matters.

4. Within possible limits, the factory should establish worker education programs according to the Ministry's published outline of worker education plans to enhance workers' knowledge and skills.

5. The factory should, to the extent possible, provide the following safety and sanitation facilities, depending on the type of industry and work conditions: (1) Safety equipment related to workers' bodies, factory buildings, machinery installations, and fire prevention. (2) Facilities such as hospitals, bathrooms, gymnasiums, and game rooms. (3) Air circulation and toxin prevention equipment in the workplace. (4) Lighting inside the factory and in worker dormitories, and toilet facilities.

6. The factory should, within possible limits, promote the following: (1) Labor insurance. (2) Savings associations. (3) Cooperatives. The benefits of the above items must be explained to the workers frequently to ensure understanding and harmonious progress.

7. On holidays, factories may convene meetings of all workers to lecture on the following topics: (1) Intellectual education. (2) Moral education. (3) Physical education.

8. The factory should, to the extent possible, provide dormitories for workers and assign staff to manage them in order to train their self-governance abilities.

9. The factory should reward workers and use a portion or all of their deserved bonuses and dividends as share capital so that workers gradually become shareholders. When issuing new shares, workers should be given priority to subscribe to deepen the alignment of interests and reduce labor-management disputes.

10. Abolish the contract labor system to prevent foremen from abusing their power and to eliminate past barriers between employers and employees. However, piecework is not subject to this restriction.

11. The factory should pay attention to the actual living conditions of workers' families and local life.

12. The factory should, to the extent possible, conduct tests with workers on the output of each machine per hour to obtain the average output. The names of the workers, raw materials, product names, and the average output should be marked on the machine. Subsequently, those whose output exceeds the original amount will be rewarded, and those whose output falls short will be penalized, thereby increasing work efficiency. However, if the production volume falls short of the original amount and it is not the worker's fault, no penalty shall be imposed.

13. Those who guide the labor movement must understand the following matters: (1) The principles of the Chinese Kuomintang Party. (2) The government's intention to protect workers. (3) The relationship between the Party and labor unions. (4) Their own mission.

Discussion 117

After the report, the chairman announced the discussion. Niu Zaikun proposed deleting the five characters "形同手續之" ("akin to procedures") in the third item of the first article of the amendment. The chairman put it to a vote, but it was rejected due to a small number of supporters. Li Quanshi proposed putting the entire proposal to a vote, and the majority agreed. The chairman then put the amendment to a vote, and it was passed by a show of hands by the entire assembly.

Adoption of the Third Group's Report 118

The chairman then stated that the discussion and report for the third group's second to thirty-third proposals (reported on the afternoon of the 4th, as seen in yesterday's newspaper) had been slightly studied by the members, and then the entire report was put to a vote and passed. Thus, all cases of the third group have been completely deliberated.

Fourth Group's Report 119

Next, the Fourth Group's review report was discussed, presented by Liu Kuidu. The results of the review of each case were divided into two parts: finance and commercial taxes, totaling three categories, summarized as follows:

Fourth Group's Review Report (A) 120

Commercial Tax Matters

The 62 proposals submitted to the Fourth Group all related to finance and commercial taxes. The group resolved to divide them into two parts for review. Apart from the financial matters reported separately, the commercial tax portion consisted of 48 proposals, all of which were reviewed on a case-by-case basis. For the convenience of discussion, they are categorized into three types and reported separately as follows:

(1) First Category: Administrative Referral Cases

All proposals whose main purpose pertains to the implementation procedures of administrative aspects are categorized by the group and compiled into simple reports. It seems unnecessary to discuss them in the general assembly. In the future, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce will refer them to the relevant authorities for verification based on the group's report. The numbers of the original proposals are as follows:

(15) Proposed Request to the National Government to Unify Egg Tax, Ji Wenquan. (28) Proposed Improvement of Porcelain Special Tax, Jiangxi Provincial Government. (29) Proposed Abolition of Dashengguan Rice Duty Bureau, Huang Zengyue. (19) Proposed Abolition of Sichuan Hardware Special Tax, Li Xingbei. (57) Proposed Abolition of Tax Stations at the Junction of Haimen and Qidong Counties, Qidong Chamber of Commerce. (14) Proposed Improvement of Procedures for Collecting Unified Cigarette Tax, Wu Tingsheng. (4) Proposed Amendment of Stamp Tax Regulations, Deng Yanhua. (24) Stamp Tax Case, Cheng Zhaodong. (62) Proposed Abolition of Chu'an Salt Surtax, Zeng Shuku. (63) Request to Guizhou Provincial Government to Abolish Exclusive Merchant Quota for Purchasing Sichuan Salt, Zeng Shuku. (38) Proposed Uniform Treatment of Chinese and Foreign Cigarette Transport Permits, Huang Zengyue. (61) Request to Stop Jiangsu Province's Business Tax Registration Fee, Wuxi and 41 other Chambers of Commerce.

(2) Second Category: Abolition of Likin Cases

All proposals related to the abuses of likin (internal transit tax) are included in this category. However, since the National Government has already issued a clear order to implement the abolition of likin on a scheduled basis, there is no need for discussion in principle. The group believes that it is only necessary to create a simple report on this desire to abolish likin and request the General Assembly to forward this report to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for submission to the National Government for early implementation. The numbers of the original proposals are as follows: (59) Request for Prompt Abolition of Likin and Tax Reduction, Chenghai County Chamber of Commerce. (60) Request for Abolition of Likin on Schedule to Save Domestic Products, Chao-Mei National Goods Industry and Commerce Joint Association. (27) Proposal to Adjust Commodity Tax Burden to Benefit the People and Maintain Domestic Goods, Wang Jie'an. (30) Proposal to Eliminate Harsh Taxes and Miscellaneous Levies to Save Domestic Goods from Danger, Wang Jie'an. (34) Exemption of Domestic Goods from Transit Taxes, Cheng Zhaodong. (37) Request for Exemption of Harsh Taxes to Protect Domestic Goods, Pan Suchu.

(3) Third Category: Discussion Cases

All proposals that, after review, have been given opinions by the group and are deemed necessary to be submitted to the General Assembly for decision are included in this category. They are combined into eleven topics as follows:

(1) National Standard Import Tariff Case 7·11·33·40·13·5·18·22·26·10· (2) National Goods Export Tariff Case 40·30·46·48· (3) Abolition of Tax Exemption and Rebate for Goods Originating from Enemy Countries 0 (4) Handling of Special Tax Principles Case 6·19·21·34·37·42·35·46·49·51·52· (5) Business Tax 21 (6) Abolition of Parcel Post Tax Case 53 (7) Tax Exemption for Handicraft Products Case 27·58· (8) Tax on Machine-Made Imitation Foreign Goods Case 34 (9) Tax Exemption for Re-Export of Imitation Machinery Case 56 (10) Uniformity of Local Taxes Within the Province Case 24 (11) Tax Reduction for Goods Manufactured by Overseas Chinese Shipped to China Case 17 (All numbers are original proposal numbers and notes)

Although the aforementioned three categories have categorized the 63 proposals separately to clarify their contents, the group's opinions on each case still require a separate, concrete report for reference during discussion. Details are provided separately below. Unfortunately, due to the different nature of each case, the order may be reversed compared to the index, which the participants are kindly asked to understand.

No. 11, Ding Changsheng proposes, "Promptly promulgate a national standard tariff." The review opinion is that the national standard tariff should adopt a protectionist policy, which is justified and should be incorporated into the import tariff case for handling.

No. 33, Cheng Zhaodong proposes, "Implement a national standard tariff." The review opinion is that increasing the import tax rate on foreign manufactured goods is justified and should be incorporated into the import tariff case for handling.

No. 40, Wang Jie'an proposes, "Reduce or exempt export tax on domestic goods and increase import tax on foreign goods." The review opinion is that the principle is justified and should be incorporated into the national standard import tariff case and the amendment of the export tariff case for handling.

No. 13, Tang Bingyuan proposes, "First implement tariff protection policies for cotton yarn and cloth." The review opinion is that the domestic cotton industry already has a foundation, and implementing a protectionist policy will surely achieve twice the result with half the effort. However, due to treaty relations, the increase can only be moderately increased within a considerable range and should be incorporated into the national standard tariff case for handling.

No. 50, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, and Fang Jiaobo propose, "Exempt export tax on domestic goods and abolish tax exemption and rebate measures for foreign goods." The review opinion is: (1) The original proposal's principle of not taxing exported goods, as well as the exceptions in categories A, B, and C, are all justified. However, whether it can be implemented in this time of financial difficulty is a matter of fact and should be incorporated into the export tariff case for handling. (2) There is no need to levy taxes on the import of raw gold. Regarding the issue of levying taxes on the import of raw silver, since the drastic fall in silver prices this year, many Chinese and foreign experts have discussed and mostly agreed that it is not appropriate to implement it before improving the currency system. As for levying taxes on the import of rice and flour, it should be determined at any time based on the domestic food supply and demand situation and should be incorporated into the national standard import tariff case for handling. (3) The practice of refunding import taxes for foreign goods exported within one year should be referred to the Ministry of Finance for cancellation.

No. 5, Deng Yanhua proposes, "Exempt locally made matches and their raw materials from taxes and duties, revise the regulations for nitric sulfur passports, and increase the import tax on imported matches." The review opinion is that, according to the current regulations on machine-made goods tax, machine-made goods transported and sold overseas are generally exempt from taxes and likin. Matches, with the approval of merchants, can be taxed as machine-made goods, and those transported and sold overseas can be exempted from export tax. The original request to increase the import tax on imported matches should be incorporated into the national standard import tariff case for handling. As for the passport issuance procedures and the explosive materials duties and taxes currently levied on match raw materials in Guangdong, the Ministry of Finance should be consulted to investigate and correct or abolish them separately.

No. 32, Cheng Zhaodong proposes, "Abolish the artificial silk tax bureau." The review opinion is that the customs duties should be corrected so that no taxes are collected again, and it should be incorporated into the national standard import tariff case. No. 34, Cheng Zhaoxiang proposes, "Exempt domestic goods from transit taxes." The review opinion is that the revision of domestic goods tax rates and the implementation of one tax per item without re-collection is extremely justified. The exemption of transit taxes should be incorporated into the abolition of likin case and reported separately to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance for implementation.

No. 37, Pan Suchu proposes, "Exempt harsh taxes to protect domestic goods." The review opinion is that the exemption of harsh taxes should be incorporated into the abolition of likin and the handling of special tax cases. As for the second and third items in the proposal, they do not fall within the scope of this group.

No. 43, Rong Zongjing and Xu Guo'an propose, "Postpone the special tax on cotton yarn." The review opinion is that the principle of the special tax on cotton yarn is justified, but it should only be implemented after the abolition of likin, and it must be handled uniformly for both Chinese and foreign products.

No. 35, Wang Jie'an proposes, "Exempt heavy taxes on the porcelain industry and dredge the transportation river." The review opinion is that implementing a one-tax-per-item system is extremely justified and should be incorporated into the abolition of likin and anti-special tax case for handling. As for dredging the transportation river, it does not fall within the scope of this group.

No. 53, the Ministry of Transportation proposes, "Abolish the parcel post tax." The review opinion is that this parcel post tax, which replaces likin, should be abolished in the list of abolitions.

No. 57, the Qidong County Chamber of Commerce of Jiangsu Province proposes, "Abolish the tax station at the junction of Haimen and Qidong Counties in Jiangsu Province." The review opinion is to incorporate it into the abolition of likin case and request the Ministry of Finance to forward the order to investigate and handle it.

No. 59, the Chenghai County Chamber of Commerce proposes, "Promptly abolish likin and reduce taxes." The review opinion is to incorporate it into the abolition of likin case for handling.

No. 60, the Chao-Mei National Goods Industry and Commerce Joint Association proposes to abolish likin. The investigation opinion is to incorporate it into the abolition of likin case for handling.

No. 7, Ding Yingfu proposes, "Exempt double taxation." The review opinion is that the original proposal focuses on refunding raw material taxes and should be handled together with other similar cases.

No. 9, Ding Changsheng proposes, "Abolish double taxation on domestic goods." The review opinion is to handle it together with other cases.

No. 17, Zhang Xiangshi et al. propose, "Tax reduction for goods manufactured by overseas Chinese and shipped to China." The review opinion is that this matter is inevitably difficult according to current tariff treaties.

No. 38, Huang Zengyue proposes, "Regarding cigarette transport permits, Chinese and foreign merchants should be treated equally." The review opinion is to propose that the General Assembly decide to have the Ministry consult with the competent authority for handling.

No. 39, Huang Zengyue proposes, "Abolish the new three-tier cigarette tax rate and restore the previous method." The review opinion is to propose that the General Assembly decide to have the Ministry consult with the competent authority for handling.

No. 61, the Wuxi and other Chambers of Commerce propose, "The business registration fee proposed by Jiangsu Province does not comply with the Ministry's regulations; please stop it." The review opinion is to propose that the General Assembly decide to have the Ministry consult with the competent authority for handling.

No. 14, Wu Tingsheng proposes, "Improve commercial taxes." The review opinion is to request a resolution from the competent authority regarding the handling of cigarette stamp affixing and transport procedures.

No. 27, Wang Jie'an proposes, "Adjust the tax burden of commodity tax." The review opinion is that the principle of exempting miscellaneous taxes on domestic goods, industrial raw materials, rice, food, salt, etc., is deemed valid. Regarding tax exemptions for handicrafts, it should be combined with proposal No. 58 for review.

No. 36, Cai Chang proposes, "Plan for commercial establishments." The review opinion is that it seems that a preliminary investigation should be conducted to determine which industries are not present in the country and must be imported from foreign countries, and then a unified plan should be made. As for the suggestion to establish a tax rate committee, the Ministry of Finance has already established a National Tariff Committee.

No. 46, Qian Yizhen proposes, "Increase export tax on soybeans and reduce inland taxes." The review opinion is that the merchants of the three northeastern provinces have already filed a case, and it should be incorporated into the export tariff case and the abolition of likin case for handling.

No. 48, Qian Yizhen proposes, "Exempt silkworm cocoon tax." The review opinion is to request a resolution from the General Assembly to have the Ministry consult and decide.

No. 49, Wang Jie'an proposes, "Levy taxes on foreign factories established in China and business tax on inland sales of foreign goods." The review opinion is that this matter is quite complex, and there are also considerations in terms of implementation. It seems appropriate to request the Ministry to consult with relevant departments for review and decision.

No. 51, Lu Xiaobo and Yu Shushen propose, "Tax exemption for daily necessities and government guarantee of interest for industrial and commercial enterprises." The review opinion is that items such as rice and cotton are large in quantity, and only using inheritance tax to compensate seems insufficient. The matter of guaranteeing interest to revitalize industry should be transferred to the fifth group.

No. 52, Lu Xiaobo and Yu Shushen propose, "Implement one tax per item; consumption taxes should not be too numerous." The review opinion is that the principle is deemed valid and should be adopted as much as possible within feasible limits.

No. 54, the Machine-Made Goods Factory Association proposes, "First remove taxes and likin from machine-made goods and refund raw material taxes." The review opinion is that even if taxes cannot be completely exempted, taxes should be reorganized and refunded on raw materials in principle, but implementation procedures will inevitably be difficult.

No. 56, Chen Dehao proposes, "Exempt re-export tax on well-made imitation machinery." The review opinion is that if the manufactured machinery is indeed well-made, it may be handled by the Special Industry Incentive Review Committee for specific review.

No. 58, the Chao-Mei National Goods Industry and Commerce Joint Association proposes, "Exempt handicraft rules." The review opinion is that the scope of so-called handicrafts should still be determined in advance. The original proposal requested a separate investigation, which is deemed necessary.

No. 4, Deng Yanhua proposes, "Amend the provisional stamp tax regulations and penalties." The review opinion is to request a resolution from the General Assembly for the Ministry to consult with the competent authority for handling.

No. 24, Cheng Zhaodong proposes, "Regarding commercial tax matters, compile opinions from various industries." The review opinion is that local taxes and levies should be uniform within a province. This opinion is valid. Regarding stamp duty, it is the same as proposal No. 4 and can be handled together.

No. 10, the Industrial and Commercial Visiting Bureau proposes, "Raw materials imported for manufacturing finished goods that are then re-exported should be given a tax refund." The review opinion is that the principle is valid, but the implementation procedures should be discussed in detail.

No. 62, Zeng Shuku proposes, "Abolish Chu'an salt surtax." The review opinion is to request a resolution from the General Assembly for the Ministry to consult with the competent authority for handling.

No. 63, Zeng Shuku proposes, "Request Guizhou to abolish the exclusive merchant quota for purchasing Sichuan salt." The review opinion is to request a resolution from the General Assembly for the Ministry to consult with the competent authority for handling.

No. 18, the Jiangxi Provincial Government proposes, "Request the Ministry of Finance to improve the special tax on porcelain to maintain the porcelain industry." The review opinion is that if a special tax on porcelain is levied after the abolition of likin, it should be levied only once, and provinces should not re-levy it. The current special tax on porcelain levied in Jiangxi Province is still a special tax, but those who have already paid the special tax in the province should not be subject to other inland taxes. It should be resolved that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce transfer it to the Ministry of Finance to strictly prohibit it. As for amending the porcelain tax rate and revising the collection method, it should be resolved that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce transfer it to the Ministry of Finance to order the Jiangxi Finance Commissioner to investigate and approve it for implementation.

No. 30, the Chinese National Goods Maintenance Association Wang Jie'an proposes, "Proposal to eliminate harsh taxes and miscellaneous levies to save domestic goods from danger." The review opinion is to incorporate it into the effort to promote the abolition of likin and transfer it to the Ministry of Finance for prompt handling.

No. 29, the Director of the Nanjing Municipal Social Bureau Huang Zengyue proposes, "Abolish the Sheng Guan sailing rice donation bureau to enrich the people's food." The review opinion is that it should be resolved that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce report it to the Executive Yuan to order the Anhui Provincial Government to abolish it within the time limit.

No. 19, Li Xingbei proposes, "Request a clear order to abolish the Sichuan hardware special tax and open transportation to benefit industry and commerce." The review opinion is that Sichuan Province's re-levy of special taxes on steel and iron and special transit donations on hardware, as well as its unauthorized ban on the export of steel and iron, all hinder the development of industry. It should be resolved that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce report it to the National Government to instruct the government to abolish the above taxes and bans within 21 years.

No. 21, the Kaifeng General Chamber of Commerce proposes, "Due to the special circumstances of Henan Province, please postpone the handling of donations and taxes to alleviate the people's difficulties." The review opinion is that Henan Province has indeed had special circumstances due to years of military operations. It should be incorporated into the abolition of likin case and handled by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce in consultation with the Ministry of Finance.

No. 6, Yuan Duanfu proposes, "Abolish likin within a time limit and exempt domestic goods raw material taxes and duties." The review opinion is that the abolition of likin has already been clearly ordered, and the government should be requested to implement it within a time limit. If taxes are levied on products, taxes on the raw materials used should also be exempted. It should be incorporated into the abolition of likin case for handling.

No. 15, Ji Wenquan proposes, "Request to use transit passes to exempt harshness and burdens to alleviate commercial difficulties and enrich the national treasury." The review opinion is that the new US tax rate has now been implemented, and its increase in the tax rate on egg imports is a matter of another country's tariff sovereignty and cannot be protested. However, it can be resolved that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce forward it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to send a letter to the ambassador to the United States to discuss methods with the United States to reduce the burden. As for the proposed use of transit passes to report and pay half of the tax upon landing and then report and pay the full export tax upon loading on a ship, it can be resolved that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce forward it to the Ministry of Finance for investigation and handling, as merchants can also apply for transit passes under the current regulations.

No. 18, Zhao Jinqing proposes, "Request to abolish various harsh levies in the interior and reduce import taxes on raw materials and increase import taxes on finished foreign goods." The review opinion is that the harsh levies and miscellaneous taxes listed in the original proposal should be incorporated into the effort to promote the abolition of likin and transferred to the Ministry of Finance for prompt handling. Also, the method of reducing import taxes on raw materials is essential for revitalizing industry. However, the items required by various industries from foreign raw materials are numerous. It should be incorporated into the national standard import tariff case, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce should investigate the types and names of foreign raw materials necessary for industry and consult the Ministry of Finance to consider granting reductions and exemptions when setting import reporting rules.

Fourth Group Review Report (B) 121

| Financial Matters |

The Fourth Group, having been entrusted to review a total of sixty-three cases, decided to divide them into two sections: finance and commerce & taxation. Apart from a separate report on matters related to commerce & taxation, there were a total of eighteen cases related to finance. Similar proposals were grouped together for joint review, resulting in nine categories: (1) currency system proposals, (2) proposal for the establishment of an industrial and commercial bank, (3) proposal for a national products bank, (4) proposal for a central bank, (5) proposal for the reorganization of industrial and commercial finance, (6) proposal for company securities and commercial paper, (7) resolutions of the International Savings Conference, (8) proposal for fundraising for industrial development, and (9) proposal for government-issued banknotes. The review opinions on each of the above cases are specifically reported as follows:

(1) Currency System Proposals

(1) Ding Changsheng's proposal to temporarily postpone the adoption of a fictitious standard currency system and to develop domestic industry and commerce to alleviate the financial crisis. (Index 2) (2) Yuan Duanfu's proposal for the national currency to adopt a gold-exchange standard. (Index 3) (3) Cai Chang's proposal to reorganize finance. (Index 45) Three proposals, one advocating for delaying the fictitious gold standard, and one advocating for adopting the gold-exchange standard. According to the opinion letter of the Ministry of Finance's Gannett, China should gradually implement the gold standard. However, the reviewers believe that this matter is of great importance and requires thorough preparation and a well-defined plan before any action is taken lightly. If there are conflicting views regarding the import and export of gold and silver this spring, it will provide speculators with a great opportunity, and merchants and people will not know what to follow, which will ultimately harm them. For the present, it is better to start by reorganizing the current complex and chaotic currency system: (1) unifying silver dollars, (2) abolishing taels and adopting dollars, (3) establishing a fixed issuance system. Then, considering the situation and weighing the circumstances, gradually adopt the gold standard. The Grand Council should quickly collaborate with the Ministry of Finance to appoint domestic experts to conduct detailed research to determine a plan and announce it as soon as possible, as the practical benefits for the national economy and people's livelihood depend on it.

(2) Proposal for the Establishment of an Industrial and Commercial Bank

(1) Deng Shanshan's proposal to establish an industrial and commercial bank to develop foreign trade. (Index 8) (2) The Shandong Agricultural and Mining Department requests a clear order stipulating that each yarn factory may borrow money from national banks at the lowest interest rate to maintain operations. (Index 20) (3) Zhou Shiguan's proposal to organize an industrial and commercial bank that seeks technical and capital cooperation, and to alleviate industry and commerce. (Index 22) Regarding the intention to establish the requested bank, existing banks such as the China Communications Bank and other banks already exist with basic scale. We should leverage and expand existing banks to meet the current financial needs of industry and commerce. Speculative ventures are not allowed in the financial industry. The Grand Council should forward the information to the Ministry of Finance, ordering all banks to fully subsidize and organize any activities that develop industry and commerce, and encourage the business of warehouse receipt financing, while strictly prohibiting speculation.

(3) Proposal for a National Products Bank

(1) Wu Jian's proposal to have the National Products Bank pilot a credit loan program so that small industrialists can obtain raw materials to produce goods. (Index 12) (2) The Jiangxi Provincial Government requests the National Products Bank to establish a branch in Jingdezhen. (Index 41) Both of the above proposals relate to the business scope of the National Products Bank. The Grand Council should notify the bank of the original proposals for consideration and implementation.

(4) Proposal for a Central Bank

(1) Li Kui'an's proposal to reorganize Southwest China's finance. (Index 16) Southwest China has suffered from years of war, and its finances are extremely chaotic. The Grand Council should review the proposal and send a letter to the Ministry of Finance, promptly working with the local authorities of the province to start reorganization, to alleviate the people's suffering.

(5) Proposal for the Reorganization of Industrial and Commercial Finance

Wang Xiaobao's proposal for the reorganization of industrial and commercial finance (Index 47). The business scope of banks is clearly stipulated by their articles of association and approved by the government. Therefore, they cannot exceed the scope. The Grand Council should forward the information to the Ministry of Finance, ordering all banks to comply with their approved articles of association.

(6) Proposal for Company Securities and Commercial Paper

(1) Liu Dajun's proposal to improve financial organization to develop industry and commerce. (Index 26) (2) Huang Shoumin's proposal to order securities exchanges to list and trade company stocks and bonds to facilitate liquidity. (Index 31) (3) Wang Jie'an's proposal to promote warehouse receipt financing to facilitate the turnover of industrial, commercial, and financial capital. (Index 23) The discount, acceptance, warehouse receipt financing, and circulation of company stocks or bonds are urgent needs for the current market in our country. The points raised in each proposal are indeed essential. The Grand Council should collaborate with the Ministry of Finance to order the banking association and the exchange federation to conduct thorough research, determine appropriate measures, and submit a report for review and approval to facilitate implementation.

(7) Proposal for the International Savings Conference

The Yunnan Construction Department's proposal to ban the International Savings Society. (Index 25) Prize-linked savings are a form of gambling that harms society, which is universally known. The government has long issued clear orders prohibiting various lotteries. However, the prize-linked savings of this type, in a disguised form of lottery, are still allowed to exist, which is regrettable. The measures proposed in this case should be unanimously supported and passed by the conference and communicated to the whole country, so the general population knows the harms.

(8) Proposal for Fundraising for Industrial Development

(1) Wang Jie'an's proposal to request the issuance of industrial development public bonds worth 100 million yuan to establish basic industries. (Index 43) (2) Cai Chang's proposal to centralize domestic capital and utilize foreign capital to develop industries. (Index 44) (3) Wang Shaotang's proposal to rescue our country's industries by advocating cooperation and accumulating funds. (Index 55) Now that the military conflict is over, it is natural to concentrate the country's economic power to promote production. Industry and commerce should cooperate to build strength. As for the revitalization of basic industries, it is possible to issue industrial development public bonds. If there are enterprises to establish, foreign capital can also be attracted. Countries worldwide often borrow foreign debts to benefit and develop industries. Our country has suffered many misfortunes, and the people are exhausted, so the construction that follows will inevitably rely on foreign capital. Now that the military conflict has ended, various facilities need to be planned. The points raised in each proposal should complement each other. To attract funds, the following points should be noted: (1) eradicate bandits and communists, reduce the military, (2) establish a budget, clarify official governance, (3) revise laws to protect human rights, (4) reorganize domestic and foreign debts, restore national credit. Once these four are in place, foreign capital can be absorbed according to the principle of equality, and used only for production enterprises. As for the production enterprises to be operated, they should be distinguished by priority and gradually implemented. Labor and capital must be taken into consideration, so that each gets what it wants. Then the future of industrial development will be promising.

(9) Proposal for Government-Issued Banknotes

Liu Mianzhi's proposal to request the government to implement the government-operated banknote exchange law. (Index 1) The matter proposed in this case is unprecedented and of great importance to the future of the economy. Judging from the established practices of various countries and the theories of the world, financial reforms should be implemented gradually. The proposer has been studying this for many years and has put in a lot of effort. The Grand Council should forward the information to the Ministry of Finance for research. The organizational proposals are very complex. My colleagues and I have limited knowledge and are ashamed to be incompetent. I hope the conference will discuss it in detail so that it can be implemented separately. I respectfully submit this for public decision. Chairman of the Fourth Group Review Committee: Bei Kanghou

Approval of Fourth Group Proposals 122

The Chairman presented the Third Category of discussion, the Commerce & Taxation section, proposal by proposal, for voting.

(1) National Fixed Import Tariff Proposal, a total of ten proposals,

(2) National Products Export Tariff Proposal, a total of four proposals, all passed.

(3) Proposal to Abolish Tax Exemptions and Rebates on Foreign Goods. Members debated the issue of imposing taxes on imported silver and imported rice and flour for a long time. Ding Jingchen argued that silver and rice imports should not be taxed, but if too much is imported, the government can order a ban. Ma Yinchu proposed to retain the proposal. Zheng Hongnian and Li Quanshi supported it. The Chairman put the retained proposal to a vote and it passed.

(4) Handling Special Tax Principles Proposal, a total of eleven proposals, all passed.

(5) Business Tax Proposal, passed.

(6) Abolish Parcel Post Tax Proposal, passed.

(7) Handmade Products Tax Exemption Proposal, a total of two proposals, passed.

(8) Machine-Made Imitation Foreign Goods Tax Proposal, passed.

(9) Tax Exemption for Re-Export of Imitation Machines Proposal, passed.

(10) Local Taxes Should be Uniform Within the Province Proposal, passed.

(11) (1) Tax Reduction for Overseas Chinese Products Transported to China Proposal, passed in principle. Members contributed many suggestions on how to reward Overseas Chinese products. The Chairman stated that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce would adopt them as much as possible. Next, the financial section was discussed. (1) Currency System Proposal, a total of three proposals, passed.

(2) Proposal for the Establishment of an Industrial and Commercial Bank, a total of three proposals. Li Zushen did not agree with the original proposal and advocated establishing a new bank. He requested that the original proposal be resubmitted for review. Some people also advocated that the original proposal be completely withdrawn. The Chairman put the resubmission for review to a vote, and it passed.

(3) Proposal for a National Products Bank, a total of two proposals, passed. (4) Proposal for a Central Bank, passed.

(5) Proposal for the Reorganization of Industrial and Commercial Finance, passed. (6) Proposal for Company Securities and Commercial Paper, passed.

(7) Regarding the International Savings Society Proposal

There was quite a lot of discussion. The result was a revision that all prize-linked savings should be banned. The banning measures should be properly formulated by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce in conjunction with the Ministry of Finance.

(8) Regarding the Proposal for Fundraising for Industrial Development

The Chairman explained that it was roughly the same as the plan and measures for issuing industrial development public bonds proposed by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. There were no objections, and it passed.

(9) Regarding the Government-Issued Banknotes Proposal

It was resolved to hand it over to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce in conjunction with the Ministry of Finance for adoption and implementation.

Discussion of the Fifth Group Report

| Passed |

First Category: Basic Industries Proposal

Second Category: Indigenous Industries Proposal

| Third Category: Today's Agenda |

At this point, the proposals of the Fourth Group had been discussed and concluded. Then the Fifth Group's review report was discussed. Hu Shuhua explained that this group was divided into six categories and gave a brief report on each category. The First Category, Basic Industries Proposal, a total of twenty-three proposals, passed. The Second Category, Indigenous Industries Proposal, a total of seventeen proposals, were discussed up to Proposal 65, Item 7, which was to deduct two jiao of foreign currency from each box of tea as a fund for improving tea. The majority opposed it and resolved to cancel it. There were still Proposals 29 and 53 and this group's Third Category, the proposal to promote national products, a total of thirty proposals. Due to the statutory time limit, they were not discussed. The plenary meeting would continue the discussion on the afternoon of the 6th, and then the meeting was adjourned.

Fifth Group Review Report 123

The Fifth Group had a total of 70 proposals. Except for Proposal 56, which the original proposer requested to be transferred to another group for review, there were 69 remaining proposals, which were divided into six categories for review.

(First Category) Basic Industries

Proposal 2, Proposal to reward the establishment of basic industries, Proposal 10, The Republic of China's acid industry should be rewarded and established by the government and the people, Proposal 33, Proposal to reward private basic industries, Proposal 51, Please vigorously reward basic industries. The above four proposals were reviewed together, and it was resolved: (1) In the reason section of Proposal 2, the various basic industries listed should be changed to words such as acid, alkali, cotton, and iron. (2) Reward measures: A. Nurture and reward according to the Special Industrial Rewards Law; B. Advance funding rewards according to the funding reward clauses of Proposal 2; C. Interest guarantee rewards according to the measures of Proposal 33, (3) the clauses were passed and the names of the nine industries listed were removed. D. Tax reduction and exemption were passed according to the measures clauses of Proposal 33, E. Freight reduction and exemption were shown according to Proposal 33 (2) passed. Subsidies and rewards were given according to the rewards methods of Proposal 52 to facilitate progress. Proposal 3, Proposal to establish a coal-making factory in Guangdong, It was resolved to request the Central Government to send personnel to jointly examine and study the Guangdong Construction Department Director to handle it. Proposal 9, The Republic of China's iron manufacturing industry should be promoted and established by the government, Proposal 11, Proposal to establish a large-scale state-owned coal and iron mine as a pioneer of the mining industry and to establish an industrial and commercial foundation, Proposal 26, Reorganize existing steel factories nationwide, Proposal 64, Quickly establish steel to consolidate the basic industry. The above four proposals were reviewed together and it was resolved that the government should establish a National Steel Industry Committee to plan the following matters: A. Reorganize existing steel factories nationwide according to Proposal 26, B. Stipulate the areas where steel factories can be established nationwide and the procedures for their establishment, C. Determine steel sales, and the government should order all agencies nationwide to purchase national products first, D. Stipulate protective tariffs and preferential freight rates, E. Restrict iron ore, scrap iron, and various metal raw materials needed for copper and iron smelting. Proposal 4, Please build a copper smelting plant. It was resolved that according to this proposal, the domestic military factories need more than 15 tons of copper per day. Since the sales channel has been determined, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce should work with the Ministry of Military Affairs to prepare for it. Proposal 69, Proposal to establish a state-owned sulfuric acid manufacturing plant, Proposal 57, Proposal to quickly build a large-scale sulfuric acid plant to benefit the people and consolidate national defense. The above two proposals were reviewed together, and it was resolved that the original proposal and plan should be sent to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for reference. Proposal 25, Establish an electrolysis green gas bleaching powder caustic soda proposal. It was resolved that green gas bleaching powder and caustic soda are important industrial products. It is proposed that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce adopt the original proposal and plan for active implementation. Proposal 50, Industrial salt proposal. It was resolved that the six proposed measures are very practical. It is proposed that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce work with the Ministry of Finance to implement them quickly. Proposal 58, Preparing a nitrogen factory proposal. It was resolved that this proposal is related to agricultural production industry and national defense. It is urgent to establish it. It is proposed that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce work with the Ministry of Agriculture and Mines and the Ministry of Military Affairs to consider adopting and actively implementing it. Proposal 32, Revitalize the sugar industry proposal, Proposal 45, Please formulate a policy to develop the sugar industry. The above two industries were reviewed together, and it was resolved to slightly supplement the original proposal plan to address the root cause and the symptoms in two steps. Regarding addressing the root cause, it is to cultivate sugar production raw materials and establish crude sugar factories. Regarding addressing the symptoms, it is to reorganize the original sugar refineries. The starting method is as follows: (1) Issue sugar industry public bonds. The sugar tax mentioned in Article 1 of the draft measures shall be used as collateral to issue public bonds to establish domestic sugar industry management, (2) Establish a sugar industry committee. Proposal 47, Improve the paper industry proposal. It was resolved to request the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to start by investigating paper raw materials. On one hand, send paper experts to various paper-producing provinces to guide and gradually improve paper technology. On the other hand, revise relevant laws to protect the national paper industry. Proposal 62, Establish a rayon manufacturing plant proposal. It was resolved that this case should be resubmitted for review, and the five members Wang Jie'an, Fan Xudong, Fang Xianting, Li Beitao, and Zhang Zilian were nominated to take charge. Proposal 34, Please promote the self-manufacturing of telecommunications materials to plug loopholes and recover profits. Proposal 51, Please promptly prepare for the manufacture of internal combustion engines. Proposal 55, It is proposed that the government find ways to promote national machine products and support machine factories. Proposal 67, Please establish a national automobile manufacturing plant. The above four proposals were reviewed together, and it was resolved to request the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to adopt and implement them.

Zheng Hongnian Strives to Reward Overseas Chinese Products 125

Industrial and commercial conference members Mei Rumei, Zhang Xiangshi, and Jiang Zhengya proposed the original proposal on granting national product treatment and tax reduction to overseas Chinese products. Four methods and six restrictions were formulated. After the review committee changed them, they were submitted to the conference. Zheng Hongnian strongly argued that this matter is of great importance to overseas Chinese. Overseas Chinese have made great contributions to the motherland. Overseas Chinese remittances reach 200 million yuan every year to make up for the trade deficit, which is the most obvious. Therefore, the conference should be requested to pass the principle of recognizing national product treatment, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce should formulate other reward measures. However, due to the hurried time, there was not enough time for discussion, and the original review plan was still passed. However, it has been recognized that rewards are necessary, and it can also be seen that Chinese people have a considerable understanding of the welfare of overseas Chinese.

Zhang Xiangshi Talks About National Consumption Case 126

Zhang Xiangsi discussed that this industrial and commercial conference was held in the capital, and various proposals reached more than 400, which were of great importance to the future of the national economy. Yang Rumei and Cai Zhengya and I jointly proposed the organization of a rationalization research association for national consumption. On the surface, it seems passive, but it is actually extremely closely related to the various production industries. The spirit of the proposal is not only to save money, but also to increase consumption efficiency, which has a direct and good impact on the solution of the food problem and indirectly saves the society capital and labor. Now the conference has passed the opinions of the review committee. Although it has submerged the spirit of the original proposal, its importance has been generally recognized. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce is willing to promote organization as soon as possible after the meeting, which can help the industrial and commercial management.

Municipal Party Headquarters Stipulates Measures to Celebrate the Premier's Birthday 132

Convene People from All Walks of Life to Hold a Celebration Meeting

Flags Will Be Hung and Business Will Be Suspended for One Day on the 12th

November 12th is the 65th anniversary of the birth of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the Premier of the Chinese Kuomintang. The Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters is actively preparing for the celebration. The celebration measures have been approved by the 65th meeting of the Municipal Executive Committee. The measures are as follows: (1) The Municipal Party Headquarters will convene four representatives from each of the city's agencies, schools, factories, party headquarters at all levels, to hold a celebration meeting at the Republic Theatre on Mingguo Road at 9:00 AM on November 12th to commemorate the 65th anniversary of the Premier's birth. (2) The Municipal Party Headquarters will prepare to hold a recreational fair to celebrate. (3) Buwan, Wusong, Zhenru, Pudong, Meilong, and other districts may convene nearby commemorative meetings and recreational fairs. (4) All sectors of the city will suspend business for one day. (5) All sectors of the city will hang flags for one day. (6) A letter will be sent to the Naval Headquarters to fire salutes in the morning and at noon on this day to mark the celebration. (7) All agencies, schools, and organizations may hold separate celebration meetings and recreational fairs. It is also reported that the recreational fair prepared by the Municipal Party Headquarters will be held at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce at Tianhougong Bridge, and the time is scheduled to start at 1:00 PM on the 12th. The programs are very exquisite. Any organization that has programs and is willing to participate can send a letter to the Municipal Propaganda Department for contact from now on.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Urges Prompt Implementation of National Tariff Regulations 133

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, Our Chamber has investigated and found that the tariff import regulations promulgated by the National Government on December 7, 1928, were implemented on February 1, 1929, with a fixed validity period of one year. Meanwhile, the National Tariff Commission was tasked with extensively revising the import regulations in preparation for their promulgation and implementation upon expiration. The initial tariff regulations largely followed the old provisions of the previous Tariff Conference in terms of tax grades, which were far from meeting protective policy requirements and urgently needed detailed revision. Subsequently, due to rising gold prices, tariffs were converted to gold units, and this validity period of the import tax, originally set for one year, had to be extended for another year. It is now reported that the draft import tax regulations proposed by the National Tariff Commission have been submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation and passage and were expected to be promulgated on National Day this month. However, after waiting for a long time, no promulgation has been seen, causing deep anxiety among the industrial and commercial sectors. Affiliated trade associations and other groups have repeatedly requested that we submit a petition urging action. We hereby report the situation in a telegram, requesting your esteemed Ministry to review and approve it, forward it to the Executive Yuan, and swiftly issue a clear order for implementation so that the nation's policy of protecting industries can be thoroughly implemented at an early date, which would be greatly beneficial to the public. Respectfully, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

A Glimpse of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Reorganization of Operations 134

Since the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company decided to become state-owned, the new Director-General, Li Zhonggong, has begun to reorganize its operations. The newly established expansion of navigation and the division of responsibilities are recorded separately as follows:

Resumption of Yangtze River Liner Service: After Li Zhonggong telegraphed to request the release of the company's Yangtze River ships leased by the Transportation Department, the Jianghua vessel returned to Shanghai yesterday. The Jiangxin and Jianguo vessels are also expected to arrive in Shanghai today. The Jiangjing vessel, which was scheduled to start service yesterday, had its boiler damaged during launching and requires repair, so the Jiangyu vessel, which has been out of service for the longest time, was assigned to replace it. Currently, among the company's Yangtze River ships, excluding the Jiangtian and Jiangda vessels, nine ships are expected to resume service from this Saturday.

Operational Division of Responsibilities in the Business Department: Director-General Li considers the Business Department to be the most important part of the entire company, with the prosperity or decline of business depending entirely on the department's proper management. With each ship about to resume operations, the internal affairs of the Business Department urgently need reform and revitalization. After yesterday's temporary meeting of the Reorganization Committee, it was decided to divide the responsibilities of the Business Department into eight sections: (1) Cargo Handling Section: Handling cargo tallying for ships and warehouses, allocating cargo to ships, and negotiating compensation for branch warehouse ships, etc.; (2) Reconciliation Section: Verifying the increase or decrease in watermen's wages and passenger expenses, and auditing the income and expenses of branch warehouses and wholesalers; (3) Inspection Section: Handling cases of watermen's wages being stolen or omitted on each ship and in each bureau, and cracking down on smuggling of private goods on each ship; (4) Statistics Section: Investigating cargo loads and compiling passenger statistics; (5) Schedule Section: Handling ship scheduling, repairs, coal, hardware, advertising, etc.; (6) Passenger Section: Handling passenger tickets, organizing passenger seating, and forwarding mail; (7) Correspondence Section: Receiving, dispatching, and storing documents; (8) Customs Declaration Section: Declaring and loading military supplies and goods, and liaising with customs. It was also stipulated that documents arriving at the department should be reviewed by the department head and deputy manager, who would then assign them to each section for handling. After receiving the documents, each section should quickly study them and submit a memorandum outlining the proposed method of handling to the department head for approval. This new method will be implemented immediately.

Continued News on Opening a Navigation Route to Weihai: In the past, the delivery of mail to Weihai was exclusively handled by British Taikoo ships. Because the British government had offices, businesses, and expatriates in Weihai, it ordered the Taikoo Company to send a ship every three days. Fearing that there would not be much cargo or passengers at the port, the British government subsidized 4,000 yuan per year to the North China Shipping Company to operate the route concurrently for carrying mail. Now that Weihai has been returned to China, this subsidy has been discontinued. The Business Department of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, in order to expand its navigation routes, had Deputy Manager He Molin draft a letter to the Post Office and submit a request to the Ministry, citing the precedent of the British government's subsidy, to request an annual subsidy of 4,000 yuan to help open a navigation route to Weihai. It is reported that this proposal has not yet been agreed to by the Post Office and will continue to be vigorously pursued in order to maintain navigational rights.

Water Rates to Be Paid at Original Rates 135

The Taxpayers' Association's Reply to the Dilong Company's Inquiry

The Dilong Company wrote: "To the Shanghai Chinese Taxpayers' Association, Regarding the water company's increase in water rates in the concession, your association and other groups have repeatedly protested and opposed it. Although the goal has not been achieved, it has been reported in the newspapers that a decision has been made to first investigate the company's accounts and then determine a solution. It also seems that a notice has been published in the newspapers to temporarily pay at the old rate. However, our company has now received the water company's bill, and the water rate is still being increased. Our company believes that since we Chinese groups have a prior agreement, how can we act alone? However, the company's bill collectors have repeatedly urged payment, which is really annoying to deal with. We are writing specifically to inquire whether we should pay or not, and we kindly ask you to provide guidance so that we can follow it for the public good. Respectfully, the accounting department of the Dilong Company, 638 Shanxi North Road, Concession, November 4th."

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Concession replied: "To the Dilong Company, We have received your letter of the 4th and are aware of everything. Since the water rate is still under investigation and has not yet been determined to be increased, all payments should be made at the original rate (i.e., 6% of the rent). The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce has already clearly implemented this, and the Shanghai Real Estate Association has also published a notice in the newspapers. Our association has also declared this to the Shanghai Waterworks Company. If the company resorts to coercion, please inform our association immediately, and our association will negotiate a solution. Your company's respect for public opinion is admirable and is worthy of emulation by our residents. We are replying accordingly. We hope you will take note."

Recent News on Yangtze River Shipping 136

Congestion of Jiangxi Goods: Due to the disturbances caused by the communists in Jiangxi Province, the central government sent troops to suppress them, causing the passenger and cargo transportation on the Nanchang-Jiujiang Railway to be suspended for some time. In the past month, there was a shortage of goods coming to and from Jiujiang. Recently, the central government's suppression troops have successively arrived in Jiangxi, and cargo transportation on the Nanchang-Jiujiang Railway has begun to recover. The downriver goods accumulated in Jiujiang have been shipped to Shanghai in large quantities since this week, and there have been telegrams urging the loading of export goods. The Yangtze River ships are competing to transport them.

Increase in Ships by the Sanbei Company: The new Ningxing vessel of the Sanbei Company in Shanghai was released by the Transportation Department yesterday and immediately dispatched to the Yangtze River. Furthermore, because there is more cargo being transported from Shanghai to the upper reaches, and the original Dexing and Changan vessels cannot yet resume service, the company has temporarily leased the 600-ton Guangji vessel from Xu Zhongxin of the Daxing Company, renaming it Guangxing. Today, it will depart from Shanghai fully loaded with Swedish matches for Hankou.

Foreign Vessels' Operations: The operations of foreign vessels on the Yangtze River, such as those of Butterfield & Swire and Jardine Matheson, are not as good as those of the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha. An investigation of the past eight days shows that the most important export cargo on the Yangtze River, cotton cloth, was carried by Nisshin Kisen Kaisha (5,606 pieces), Butterfield & Swire (2,686 pieces), and Jardine Matheson (1,849 pieces). The second most important cargo, white sugar, was carried by Nisshin Kisen Kaisha (23,785 bags), Butterfield & Swire (11,221 bags), and Jardine Matheson (8,338 bags). Kelp was carried by Nisshin Kisen Kaisha (9,325 pieces), Jardine Matheson (2,164 pieces), and Butterfield & Swire (914 pieces). Cigarettes were carried by Jardine Matheson (3,547 boxes), Nisshin Kisen Kaisha (2,540 boxes), and Butterfield & Swire (811 boxes). In the past, Butterfield & Swire had a monopoly on the transportation of longans and lychees on the Yangtze River, but since last month, Nisshin Kisen Kaisha vessels have also been carrying these goods. The rapid progress of Japanese shipping can be seen from this.

Director Yuan Expresses Gratitude to the Rokko Maru for Rescuing Fishermen 137

On the 20th of last month, a fishing boat was caught in a storm outside the Wusong port and capsized. Seven fishermen, including Yan Linkui, were in danger of drowning. Fortunately, the Rokko Maru passed by and did its best to rescue them, bringing them to Shanghai. After they arrived in Shanghai, Director Yuan Liang of the Public Security Bureau dispatched police officers to properly resettle the victims and provided them with travel expenses to return to their hometowns. Director Yuan sent a letter to the Japanese Consul General, Shigemitsu Aoi, yesterday to express his gratitude. Director Yuan also sent thank-you certificates to the captain and crew members of the Rokko Maru who contributed to the rescue to recognize their efforts.

(2) In accordance with the county government's order to send personnel to Chenhang to inspect and accept the new house of the Fifth District Office and the Security Corps, Chief Gong of the Technical Section was instructed to go on November 1 to conduct the inspection and acceptance. A reply has been submitted to the county government for filing. (3) The list of committee members of the Yu Tang River Dredging Preparatory Committee has been submitted by the committee and appointments have been made separately and instructions have been issued to the committee for distribution. The following resolutions were then passed on the following cases: (1) How to handle the case of the transportation company's application for registration of the Shanghai-Minhang-Nantuo long-distance bus line? It was decided to transfer it to the county government meeting. (2) Case of scheduling the measurement of Tangbei Road: It was decided to send Director Huang of the Highway Department and Chief Gong of the Technical Section to measure it on the 10th of this month and notify the Second and Third Districts for inspection. (3) Should personnel be sent to investigate whether to register various shipping companies that come to the bureau one after another? It was decided to send Chief Gong to conduct a thorough investigation on a specified date. (4) The Chun Shen Tang River Dredging Committee submitted a request to summarize and send the Chun Shen Tang River Dredging budget proposal. It was decided to convene a meeting with the Shanghai Port Authority and the Songjiang County Construction Bureau on a scheduled date to discuss and handle the matter.

Italian Consulate Prepares to Celebrate National Day 147

Italy's National Day is on the 11th of this month. It is reported that the Italian Consulate in Shanghai will hold a reception at the consulate at noon on that day, inviting party, government, and military leaders from China, as well as the consular corps, to celebrate the occasion.

China & Foreign Telephone Company Plans to Expand Pudong Lines 148

Shanghai Bureau Will Prevent Cables from Landing on the East Bank

The Ministry of Communications is actively planning to recover the telephones installed by the China & Foreign Telephone Company in the Chinese area, but the China & Foreign Company has recently intensified its efforts. An investigation revealed that the company's telephones in Pudong originally used underwater cables laid under the Huangpu River to connect to the east bank. The entire line has 75 pairs. Currently, the company has replaced the old cables, which have been damaged over the years, with new cables containing 150 pairs, which is twice as many as before. It is reported that the Shanghai Telephone Bureau has reported this to the Ministry of Communications and has stated that in order to facilitate business contacts, it will allow the company to maintain its existing operations until the Pudong branch bureau is established. However, if the company wants to expand its lines, the Shanghai Bureau will prevent its cables from landing on the east bank.

Additional Military Equipment for Railway Station Protection 149

Due to the approach of the winter defense season, the Shanghai-Jiashan section of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Police Department urgently needs to strengthen protection. The old and new cargo warehouses at the South Station are located in a vast area, and the Riyuegang Station is close to the branching waterways of the Huangpu River and has a large amount of cargo. The North Station material depot is located in an open field. Additional police officers must be assigned to patrol these key locations. However, the original firearms used by the section are insufficient to meet the needs. Therefore, Zhuang Shouhua, the police chief of the section, submitted a request to the two railway police headquarters for the allocation of ten additional firearms and pistols for the winter defense period for use in protecting commercial goods.

Wuling Ship Attacked by Bandits En Route to Hankou 150

The bandits in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River are now fleeing upstream. There are still traces of bandits lurking along the river above Shashi. This time, the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha's Wuling Maru was attacked by bandits after passing Shashi on its way from Shanghai to Yichang. The Japanese Navy stationed on the ship opened fire with machine guns, firing 400 rounds at the bandits on both banks, and the bandits were finally dispersed. Unexpectedly, when the ship was returning to Shanghai from Yichang, it encountered a large number of bandits again as it approached Shashi. As the ship sped downstream, it was fired upon by bandits with several cannons. The Wuling Maru was hit by two shells. Fortunately, the shells were made of rotten nails and scrap iron and were old-fashioned earthen cannons, so the firing power was very weak. Although the ship's hull was slightly damaged, the crew and passengers were safe and sound, only suffering a scare. Later, the Navy stationed on the ship fired 300 rounds of machine gun fire, and only then were the bandits repelled. The ship is expected to arrive in Shanghai today.

Dapu Guardian Police Killed: Yesterday, a passenger from Dinghai arrived in Shanghai and told reporters that the Jintang Li Port of Dinghai was looted by pirates, and the Dapu merchant ship from Ningbo to Dinghai was carrying passengers and sailed to the mouth of Dapu when it encountered more than a dozen pirates with wooden guns who fired at the ship. The ship's guard police came out to fight back and two of them were shot dead by the bandits and their bodies were abandoned in the sea. The bandits took over the ship and ordered the crew to take the bandits to Li Port for looting. The entire city was robbed and no one escaped. Four members of the local defense team were shot and killed by bandits and their military equipment was seized. Then they looted the stolen goods and boarded pirate ships, escaping by sea.

Charity Group Assets Must Not Be Changed Without Authorization 151

Nor May There Be Any Concealment or Failure to Report

The Shanghai Municipal Government issued a notice yesterday, stating: "Notice regarding the fact that the Social Affairs Bureau reported that the Charity Group Property Reorganization Committee reported that committee members such as Mo Heng proposed at the fifth regular meeting that cases of charity groups changing property without authorization and concealing or failing to report should be handled as follows. After deliberation, it was resolved to submit a request to the municipal government to issue a notice for all charity groups to comply with: (1) No property may be changed without authorization during the reorganization period; (2) All property of each charity group must be reported truthfully to the committee. Any false or incomplete reporting will be severely punished. An investigation revealed that charity groups changing property without authorization is a violation of the law and creates many malpractices. Since the establishment of the committee, it has begun to promote the reorganization of the property of various charity groups. If each charity group must change property, it should wait until the committee's reorganization is completed before handling the matter appropriately. Furthermore, the committee's investigation of the property of charity groups in the city should be as detailed as possible and should not omit anything. However, each charity group may have a considerable history and the staff has been replaced several times, and there may be omissions in the transfer of responsibility. Or the management may be improper, and public property has been converted into private property. Therefore, if there are cases of false reporting, the committee's eyes and ears may not be able to see everything. If a warning is not issued in advance, it will be difficult to handle in the future and will have a great impact on charity work. Therefore, we must report this matter. We respectfully request your approval and transfer it for implementation. Furthermore, before the reorganization of the property of each charity group is completed, it will be temporarily suspended. This has been approved by the Fifth One Five Directive of the Finance Bureau and has been notified to all charity groups for compliance. The committee's regulations also have strict provisions that all property of each charity group must be reported truthfully. The committee's request is to prevent the occurrence of disputes and avoid obstacles to the reorganization, which is not without reason. Therefore, we have prepared a document to report and respectfully request your review and approval to issue a notice for implementation, which is in the public interest. Therefore, an investigation revealed that the property of charity groups is the foundation of relief work. Unauthorized disposal is a violation of the law and creates many malpractices. Before the reorganization is completed, all changes will be temporarily suspended. This was previously announced. According to the previous report, it is appropriate to announce to all that they must comply and must not change anything without authorization or conceal or fail to report it, which may cause inconvenience. Sincerely announce."
